  相关词：
  **<u>peep/ peek</u> at……** 偷窥……
  **leer at……** 色迷迷地看……
  ✎ He was always <u>leering at</u> female members of staff. 他总是色迷迷地看女职员。
  **glance at……** 匆匆地看一眼（有意）
  **glimpse……** vt. 无意中一眼瞥见……（无意）
  **gaze at……** 看得出神,充满兴趣地凝视（表示被看的事物非常好看）（L6，下同）
  **stare at……** 瞪大了眼睛凝视
  **gape at……** 张着嘴傻看
  **glare at……** 怒目而视


### 🕹️ **课文讲解**
+ **much-travelled** 游历广的（**much** 表示很多人参与的，广为……，广受……）
  **much-loved** 备受爱戴的
  **much-respected** 备受尊敬的
  **much-admired** 备受钦佩的
  **much-discussed** 广为讨论的
  **much-criticized** 备受批评的
  **much-acclaimed** 备受赞誉的
+ **assume** v. 假定（贬义，通常指没有证据，暗示是错的、不合理的）
  ✎ Up to now, historians have <u>assumed</u> that calendars came into being with the advent of agriculture, for then man was faced with a real need to understand something about the seasons.（L38）
  ✎ When lights fuse, furniture gets rickety, pipes get clogged, or vacuum cleaners fail to operate, some women <u>assume</u> that their husbands will somehow put things right.（L46）
+ **remote** places 偏僻的，~~远的~~
+ **cut…… off from……** 使……与……隔绝
  英文释义：to prevent sb./ sth. from leaving or reaching a place or communicating with people outside a place
  ✎ Having a new baby can <u>cut</u> a young mother <u>off from</u> the adult world. 有小孩之后，年轻的母亲就与成人世界隔绝了。（主动）
  ✎ Accessible only by air, the town <u>is cut off from</u> the rest of the country. 这座城镇只能乘飞机进入，与全国其他地区隔绝。（被动）
  ✎ Except for one or two places such as Zermatt and Chamonix, which had rapidly become popular, Alpine villages tended to be impoverished settlements <u>cut off from</u> civilization by the high mountains.（B4L3-作非谓语）
  同义替换：
  **be out of touch with……** 与……失去联系；不了解……
  **keep in touch** 保持联络
  ✎ We’ve <u>been out of touch with</u> Roger for years now. 我们已经和罗杰失去联系很多年了。
  ✎ Old people sometimes <u>are out of touch with</u> the modern world. 老年人有时与现代世界脱节。
  **separate…… from……** 把（前者）与（后者）隔离（**se-**：分开；**par**：part）
  ✎ <u>Separating</u> prisoners <u>from</u> each other is sometimes the only way of preventing riots. 将囚犯彼此分开有时是防止暴乱的唯一方法。
  ✎ After having been wounded towards the end of the war, he had been sent to hospital and <u>was separated from</u> his unit.（L36）
  **isolate…… from……** 把……与……隔离
  ✎ A high wall <u>isolated</u> the house <u>from</u> the rest of the village. 一堵高墙把房子和村里的其他地方隔开了。
  ✎ When a person has an infectious disease, he <u>is</u> usually <u>isolated from</u> other people. 当一个人患有传染病时，他通常会与其他人隔离开来。
  **segregate…… from……**（因种族，性别，宗教等原因）把……与……隔离（仅指人）
  ✎ a culture in which women <u>are segregated from</u> men 男女隔离的文化
  ✎ Blacks <u>were segregated from</u> whites in schools. 黑人在学校里与白人隔离。
+ **one’s (fellow) countryman** 某人的同胞
  **= one’s compatriot**（**patr**：与爸爸相关）
  ✎ a hero much loved by <u>his countrymen</u> 深受同胞爱戴的英雄
  ✎ Didn’t he feel guilty about betraying <u>his fellow countrymen</u>? 他背叛同胞难道不感到内疚吗？
  ✎ Chris Robertson of Australia beat <u>his compatriot</u> Chris Dittmar in the final. 澳大利亚选手克里斯·罗伯逊在决赛中击败了他的同胞克里斯·迪特马尔。
  **one’s fellow <u>Chinese/ Americans/ ……</u>** 中国同胞们/美国同胞们
  ✎ And so, <u>my fellow Americans</u>, ask not what your country can do for you; ask what you can do for your country. 因此，我的美国同胞们，不要问你的祖国能为你做什么，要问你能为你的祖国做什么。（肯尼迪）
+ **can be** 有可能（表推测）

#### 👾 **as 引导的非限定性定语从句与 which 引导的非限定性定语从句的区别**
（复制自L33）
1. **as 作为关系代词指代整个主句，而 which 作为关系代词指代整个主句或先行词均可；**
2. **as 引导的非限定性定语从句位于主句前、中、后均可，而 which 引导的非限定性定语从句不能位于主句之前；**
as 引导的非限定性定语从句几乎是唯一一个可以放在主句前面的定语从句。
✎ <u>As a poet points out</u>, life is but a dream. 正如一位诗人指出的，人生不过是一场梦。（前）
✎ Children, <u>as/ which is always the case</u>, love their mother. 孩子们总是会爱自己的母亲。（中）
✎ She became angry, <u>as/ which many could see</u>. 她生气了，正如许多人所看到的。（后）
3. **as 引导的非限定性定语从句含有“众所周知”的意思，常译为“正如……”，而 which 引导的非限定性定语从句则未必有这个意思；**
✎ The sun heats the earth, <u>which makes it possible for plants to grow</u>. 太阳加热地球，使植物生长成为可能。
4. **在“as + is/was + done”结构中可省略“is/was”，而在“which + is/was + done”结构中，则要省略“which + is/was”，而不能只省略be动词。**
✎ <u>As (is) reported</u>, a foreign delegation will visit the city. 正如被报道的那样，一个外国代表团将访问该市。
+ 例句
  ✎ Things can go wrong on a big scale, <u>as</u> a number of people recently discovered in Parramatta, a suburb of Sydney.（L33）
  ✎ <u>As</u> the Commanding Officer explained later, one half of the station did not know what the other half was doing!（B2L91）
  ✎ If, <u>as</u> has been reported, they have protected humans from sharks, it may have been because curiosity attracted them and because the scent of a possible meal attracted the sharks.（B4L18）
  ✎ <u>As</u> is so often pointed out, knowledge is a two-edged weapon which can be used equally for good or evil.（B4L22）

#### 👾 **of + 名词：描述人或事物的特征**
（L32复习）
1. **做后置定语（比用形容词更正式）。**
2. **在系动词后做表语（同样比用形容词更正式）。**
   
┏ Nothing <u>of value</u> was found, but the numerous items which were brought to the surface proved to be <u>of great interest</u>.（L32）
┗ Nothing <u>valuable</u> was found, but the numerous items which were brought to the surface proved to be <u>very interesting</u>.（还原为形容词）
┏ These attracted many visitors, for they were not only <u>of great architectural interest</u>, ……（本文）
┗ These attracted many visitors, for they were not only <u>architecturally interesting</u>, ……

+ **contain** （箱子、篮子、碗）里装了东西；在建筑物里面有东西
  ✎ The museum <u>contains</u> a number of original artworks. 博物馆收藏了许多原创艺术品。
  ✎ The room was small and <u>contained</u> far too much furniture. 房间很小，放了太多家具。
+ **beautifully**
  + ad1. 美丽地，漂亮地 in a beautiful way
    ✎ They had large rooms with <u>beautifully</u> decorated walls.（L3）
    ✎ Diamond necklaces and rings had been <u>beautifully</u> arranged on a background of black velvet.（L6）
  + ad2. 很好地 very well（本文义）
  ✎ My leg has healed <u>beautifully</u>. 我的腿恢复得很好。
  ✎ The children behaved <u>beautifully</u>. 孩子们表现得很好。
  ✎ Imagine their dismay when they found a <u>beautifully</u>-cooked wallet and notes turned to ash!（L7）
> 仿写第2段第2句
  故宫(the Imperial Palace)吸引了很多游客，因为它不但在建筑方面很有趣，而且里面有大量的保存完好的文物(historical relic)。
  The Imperial Palace attracts many visitors, for it is not only of great architectural interest, but contains a large number of beautifully preserved historical relics as well.
+ 名词短语本身就可以作时间状语，此处的on可去掉。注：today不能说on today，tomorrow不能说on tomorrow。
  ✎ <u>(On) the day before our departure</u>, several bus loads of tourists descended on the town.（本文）
  ✎ <u>The day after the birth of the five children</u>, an aeroplane arrived in Aberdeen bringing sixty reporters and photographers.（L45）
  ┏ We met <u>on the following day</u>. 转天，我们相会了。
  ┗ We met <u>the following day</u>.
  ┏ We met <u>in the spring of 1983</u>.
  ┗ We met <u>the spring of 1983</u>.
+ **load** 一车，一船，……（量词，指人指物都可）
  ✎ a truck <u>load</u> of wood 一卡车的木材
  ✎ a ship <u>load</u> of cotton 一船的棉花
  ✎ a car <u>load</u> of visitors 一车的访客
+ **descend <u>on/ upon</u>……**（L41）
  1. to visit sb./sth. in large numbers, esp. unexpectedly or inconveniently 大批突然到来
    ✎ Millions of tourists <u>descend upon</u> the area every year. 每年有数百万游客涌入该地区。
    ✎ Crowds of tourists <u>descended on</u> the tiny church. 成群结队的游客涌向这座小教堂。
  2. (of night, darkness, a mood, etc.) to arrive and begin to affect sb./sth., esp. suddenly （黑暗，夜色，某种情绪等）突然降临
    ✎ Total silence <u>descended on</u> the room. 房间里突然陷入一片沉寂。/房间里的人们突然间都不说了。
    ✎ Calm <u>descended upon</u> the crowd. 人群突然陷入一片平静。
    ✎ Few things could be more impressive than the peace that <u>descends on</u> deserted city streets at weekends when the thousands that travel to work every day are tucked away in their homes in the country.（L41）
+ **be more than…… <u>can/ could</u>……**  是……不能/无法……的（L43）
  ✎ Dancing proved to be <u>more than</u> the dish <u>could bear</u>, for during the party it capsized and sank in seven feet of water.（L43）
  ✎ The pain <u>is more than</u> I <u>can</u> bear. 这个疼痛是我无法忍受的。
  ✎ The story <u>is more than</u> I <u>can</u> believe. 这个故事是我无法相信的。
  ✎ The beauty of the West Lake is <u>more than</u> words <u>can</u> describe. 西湖的美丽是语言无法描述的。
  ✎ Such a complicated situation <u>is</u> far <u>more than we could</u> anticipate and deal with. 这种复杂的局势远远超出了我们的预期和应对能力。
+ **take** v.  取道…… use (a road, path, etc) as a route to go to a place
  ✎ I usually <u>take</u> the M6 when I go to Scotland. 我到苏格兰去通常都取道6号高速公路。
+ **lead** v. 通往…… to go in a particular direction or to a particular place 
  ✎ The path <u>led down to</u> a small lake. 这条小路向下通往一个小湖。
  ✎ This door <u>leads into</u> the garden. 这扇门通往花园。
  ✎ We followed a dirt track <u>leading through</u> the woods. 我们沿着一条穿过树林的土路走过去。
  ✎ The road <u>leads west</u> for three miles, then turns south. 这条路向西延伸三英里，然后向南转弯。
+ **wood** [U] 木头；[C] 树林
+ **<u>trace/ weave/ wind</u> one’s way** 蜿蜒前进（L42）
  ✎ Highway 99 <u>winds its way</u> along the coast. 99号公路沿着海岸蜿蜒而行。
  ✎ Lori spotted them as they <u>weaved their way</u> through the tables. 当他们在桌子间蜿蜒穿梭时，洛里发现了他们。
+ ┏ **<u>have no idea</u> that/ how/ what/ why/ which/ where/ ……**
  ┏ **<u>not have any idea</u> that/ how/ what/ why/ which/ where/ ……**（语气更重）
  ┗ 不知道……
  ✎ He <u>had no idea</u> (that) she was like that. 他不知道她原来是那样的一个人。
  ✎ She <u>doesn’t have any idea</u> where they’ve gone. 她完全不知道他们去了哪里。
  ✎ They <u>had no idea</u> what time they were supposed to arrive. 他们不知道他们会在何时到来。
+ **moor** v. 停泊（大船小船都可）
  ✎ We <u>moored</u> alongside the quay. 我们在码头旁停泊。（不及物）
  **moor…… to……** 停泊在某地（及物）
  ✎ We <u>moored</u> the boat <u>to</u> a large tree root. 我们把船系泊在一棵大树的树根上。
  ✎ A number of fishing boats <u>were moored to</u> the quay. 很多渔船系泊在码头。
  相关词：
  **anchor**（L28）
  v. 抛锚，停泊（多指大船）
  ✎ They <u>anchored</u> the ship in the harbour. 他们把船停泊在了港口。（及物）
  ✎ The ship <u>anchored</u> in the harbour. 这艘船停泊在了港口。（不及物）
  ✎ Before she had <u>anchored</u>, the men from the boats had climbed on board and……（L28）
  n. 锚
  ┏ **<u>cast/ drop</u> anchor** 抛锚
  ┗ **<u>weigh anchor/ set sail</u>** 起锚；启航
  ✎ We <u>dropped anchor</u> a few yards offshore. 我们在离岸几码处抛锚。
  ✎ The next morning, they <u>weighed anchor</u> and began to move south again. 第二天早上，他们起锚，继续向南行进。
+ ┏ In it there was a boatman fast asleep.（原文）
  ┗ In it there was a boatman <u>who was</u> fast asleep.（补全定语从句）
  关系代词后如果跟be动词，两者可同时去掉。
+ **be <u>fast/ sound</u> asleep** 熟睡（fast/ sound 是副词；asleep 是形容词）
  **= be sleeping <u>deeply/ soundly/ tight</u>**（sleeping 是动词；deeply/ soundly/ tight 是副词）

**ferry**
  n. 渡船；渡口
  v. 运送（人或货物）to carry people or goods between two or more places 
  ✎ <u>ferry</u> goods <u>to</u> the mainland 将货物运往大陆
  ✎ Can you <u>ferry</u> us <u>across</u>? 你能渡我们过去吗？
+ **be <u>reluctant/ unwilling</u> to do sth.** 不愿意做某事（固定搭配）
+ **persuade sb. <u>to do/ into doing</u> sth.** 说服某人做某事（L26）
+ **be perched on……** 位于比较高且危险的地方（L43）
  ✎ For one agonizing moment, the dish <u>was perched</u> precariously <u>on</u> the bank of the canal, but it suddenly overbalanced and slid back into the water.（L43）
  ✎ a house <u>perched on</u> a cliff above the town 坐落在城镇上方悬崖上的房子
+ **straggle** v. 无规则地或散乱地生长或散布 grow or spread in an irregular or untidy manner
  ✎ Unpainted wooden buildings <u>straggle</u> along the main road out of town. 沿着出城的主干道散落着一些未上漆的木制建筑。
  ✎ a <u>straggling</u> village 一个布局分散的村庄
  ✎ vines <u>straggling</u> over the fences 篱笆上蔓生的藤蔓
  近义替换：
  **winding, tortuous** （道路、河流等）蜿蜒的
  ✎ The road is <u>tortuous</u>, but the prospects are bright. 道路是曲折的，但前途是光明的。
+ **line** v. 沿某物排成行 form a line along sth.
  ┏ Tall trees <u>line</u> the road on either side. 高大的树在路两旁排成行。（主动）
  ┗ The road <u>is lined with/ by</u> tall trees on either side.（被动）
+ 逻辑主语 + 非谓语动词 = 独立主格结构
+ **sign of life** 生命的迹象
+ **a. + -looking** 看起来……的
  ✎ a very <u>modern-looking</u> woman（L3）
  ✎ an <u>interesting-looking</u> carved dagger（L34）
  ✎ the <u>sorry-looking</u>, blackened figure（L35）
  ✎ an <u>ugly-looking</u> black goat（本文）
+ **on** 用……拴着
  ✎ Please keep your dog <u>on</u> a leash. 请用皮带拴住你的狗。
+ length n. 长度；一根，一截，一段
 ✎ Each of the four cables contains 26,108 <u>lengths</u> of wire.（L17）
+ **tie** v.拴，系，捆，绑（L16）
  ✎ She kept it <u>tied to</u> a tree in a field during the day and went to fetch it every evening.（L16）
+ **nearby** ad. 在附近（L40、41）
  ✎ The student hid in an archway <u>nearby</u> where he could watch and hear everything that went on.（L40）
+ ┏ The village seemed deserted, the only sign of life being an ugly-looking black goat on a short length of rope tied to a tree in a field nearby.（原文-独立主格结构-重点突出、简洁）
  ┗ The village seemed deserted, <u>and</u> the only sign of life <u>was</u> an ugly-looking black goat on a short length of rope tied to a tree in a field nearby.（原文改-并列句）
  ✎ 这本书很无聊(boring)，唯一有趣的部分是它的封皮。
  The book is boring, the only interesting part being its cover.
  ✎ 箱子(chest)里的东西(contents)令人失望，唯一有价值的发现是一柄看起来有趣的雕花的匕首。
  The contents of the chest were disappointing, the only valuable find being an interesting-looking carved dagger.
+ ┏ **all at once** 突然（**at once** 立刻）
  ┗ **suddenly**
  ┗ **all of a sudden**
+ **alarm** n. 惊慌，恐慌 a feeling of fear or worry because sth. bad or dangerous might happen
  ✎ She looked up <u>in alarm</u>. 她惊恐地抬头看。
  ✎ Scientists have said <u>there is no cause for alarm</u>. 科学家们表示，没有理由恐慌。
+ **be filled with** <u>anger/ fear/ dread/ horror/ joy/ happiness/ doubt/ alarm/ revulsion/ admiration/ remorse/ ……</u> 充满某种情绪（L28、L39）
  ✎ Their faces <u>were</u> suddenly <u>filled with fear</u>. 他们的脸上突然充满了恐惧。
  ✎ I <u>am filled with admiration</u> for your bravery. 我非常钦佩你的勇敢。
  ✎ Knowing that the industrious ant lives in a highly organized society does nothing to prevent us from <u>being filled with revulsion</u> when we find hordes of them crawling over a carefully prepared picnic lunch.（L54）
+ ┏ **offer sb. sth.**
  ┗ **offer sth. to sb.**
+ **be shy of……** 对……腼腆羞怯；害怕……
  ✎ Children <u>are</u> often <u>shy of</u> people they don’t know. 孩子们经常对他们不认识的人感到害羞。
  ✎ I<u>’m shy of</u> buying shares, in case I lose money. 我不敢买股票，以防赔钱。
  ✎ Once bitten, twice shy. 一朝被蛇咬，十年怕井绳。（谚语）
+ 名词前面有量词时，如果量词需形容词修饰，则形容词要放在量词之前（L15、L39）
  ✎ a <u>nice</u> cup of tea 一杯好茶
  ✎ a <u>beautiful</u> stretch of field 一片美丽的原野
  ✎ a <u>stagnant</u> pool of water 一潭死水
  ✎ For most of them, 50 pence is a small price to pay for a <u>nice big</u> bar of chocolate.（L15）
  ✎ Our next obstacle was a <u>shallow</u> pool of water about half a mile across.（L39）
  ✎ When we later walked down the main street of the village, we were followed by a <u>silent</u> procession of children.（本文）
+ **come to life** 变活跃起来 to become more interesting, exciting or full of activity
  ✎ The match finally <u>came to life</u> in the second half. 比赛终于在下半场活跃起来了。
  ✎ You’re very cool with your brother, but with your friends you really <u>come to life</u>. 你跟你哥哥在一块时比较高冷，但和你的朋友在一起时，你真的挺活跃的。
+ 【✔】Faces appeared at windows.（原文-传神）
  【◐】People looked out of the window.（单调）
  ↓ She smiled.（描述越来越具体、传神）
  ↳ A smile appeared on her lips.
  ↳ Her lips curved into a smile.
  ↳ Her rosy lips curved into a gentle smile.
+ **in shirt sleeves = shirt-sleeves** 只穿衬衣的
  英文释义：dressed informally without wearing anything, such as a jacket, over a shirt
+ **doorway** 门口
+ **there is no <u>doubt/ question</u> that……** 毫无疑问的是……（L25）
  ✎ <u>There is no doubt that</u> if she had not lost her rudder she would have won the race easily.（L25）
  ✎ <u>There is no question that</u> the government knew about the deal.
+ **quicken one’s pace** 加快脚步
  ✎ He <u>quickened his pace</u>, longing to be home. 他加快了脚步，盼望回家。
  ✎ Thinking that she was being followed, she <u>quickened her pace</u>. 她认为被跟踪了，就加快了脚步。
+ **make one’s way** 前往某地（常跟介词短语搭配）（L15、L36、L42）
  ✎ I <u>made my way</u> <u>to the house</u>. 我朝房子走了过去。
  ✎ I <u>made my way</u> <u>into the backyard</u>. 我走进了后院。
  ✎ I <u>made my way</u> <u>along the river</u>. 我沿着河走去。
  ✎ I <u>made my way</u> <u>up the stairs</u>. 我走上了楼。
  ✎ The hospital had been bombed and Hans <u>had made his way</u> back <u>into Western Germany</u> on foot.（L36）
  ✎ Turning back down the main street, we quickened our pace and <u>made our way</u> rapidly <u>towards the stream</u> where we hoped the boatman was waiting.（本文）

#### 👾 **嵌入式定语从句（Embedded Attributive Clause） <span id="⚓嵌入式定语从句2">（🪐）</span><a href="#⚓嵌入式定语从句">（🚀L42）</a>**
**特征：既修饰先行词，同时又做另一个主谓结构的宾语。**
✎ She has an adopted son <u>who **she says** is an orphan</u>. 她有一个养子，据她说他是个孤儿。
✎ Aleko suddenly acquired a new lamb <u>which **he claimed** was bought</u>. 阿列科突然获得了一只新羊羔，他声称这只羊羔是买来的。
✎ In this part of the cave, they could hear an insistent booming sound <u>which **they found** was caused by a small waterspout shooting down into a pool from the roof of the cave</u>.（L42）
↳ 解析：划线部分一方面修饰水声，另一方面作加粗部分的宾语。
┏ Turning back down the main street, we quickened our pace and made our way rapidly towards the stream <u>where we hoped the boatman was waiting</u>.（原文-定语从句）
┗ Turning back down the main street, we quickened our pace and made our way rapidly towards the stream, <u>and we hoped that the boatman was waiting there</u>.（相当于并列句）
在英语水平低的时候，语法是重点；英语水平中级以上，句法是重点；英语水平再高，则是单词量。单词量小，不可能表达得传神、精确。

---

## **Lesson 49 - The ideal servant**
### **课文原文** [🌏](#第三册目录)
<font color=gray size=4>It is a good thing my aunt Harriet died years ago. If she were alive today she would not be able to air her views on her favourite topic of conversation: domestic servants. Aunt Harriet lived in that leisurely age when servants were employed to do housework. She had a huge, rambling country house called ‘The Gables’. She was sentimentally attached to this house, for even though it was far too big for her needs, she persisted in living there long after her husband’s death. Before she grew old, Aunt Harriet used to entertain lavishly. I often visited The Gables when I was a boy. No matter how many guests were present, the great house was always immaculate. The parquet floors shone like mirrors; highly polished silver was displayed in gleaming glass cabinets; even my uncle’s huge collection of books was kept miraculously free from dust. Aunt Harriet presided over an invisible army of servants that continuously scrubbed, cleaned, and polished. She always referred to them as ‘the shifting population’, for they came and went with such frequency that I never even got a chance to learn their names. Though my aunt pursued what was, in those days, an enlightened policy, in that she never allowed her domestic staff to work more than eight hours a day, she was extremely difficult to please. While she always criticized the fickleness of human nature, she carried on an unrelenting search for the ideal servant to the end of her days, even after she had been sadly disillusioned by Bessie.

Bessie worked for Aunt Harriet for three years. During that time she so gained my aunt’s confidence, that she was put in charge of the domestic staff. Aunt Harriet could not find words to praise Bessie’s industriousness and efficiency. In addition to all her other qualifications, Bessie was an expert cook. She acted the role of the perfect servant for three years before Aunt Harriet discovered her ‘little weakness’. After being absent from the Gables for a week, my aunt unexpectedly returned one afternoon with a party of guests and instructed Bessie to prepare dinner. Not only was the meal well below the usual standard, but Bessie seemed unable to walk steadily. She bumped into the furniture and kept mumbling about the guests. When she came in with the last course — a huge pudding — she tripped on the carpet and the pudding went flying through the air, narrowly missed my aunt, and crashed on the dining table with considerable force. Though this caused great mirth among the guests, Aunt Harriet was horrified. She reluctantly came to the conclusion that Bessie was drunk. The guests had, of course, realized this from the moment Bessie opened the door for them and, long before the final catastrophe, had had a difficult time trying to conceal their amusement. The poor girl was dismissed instantly. After her departure, Aunt Harriet discovered that there were piles of empty wine bottles of all shapes and sizes neatly stacked in what had once been Bessie’s wardrobe. They had mysteriously found their way there from the wine cellar!</font>


### 🌻 **单词讲解**
+ **rambling** a. 不规则的，布局凌乱的
  （尤指建筑物、街道、城镇等）无规则地向各方延伸的，布局凌乱的
  英文释义：(esp. of buildings, streets, towns, etc.) extending in various directions irregularly
  ✎ She had a huge, <u>rambling</u> country house called ‘The Gables’.（本文）
  **ramble** v.&n. 漫步，闲逛
  ✎ I like <u>rambling</u> in the country. 我喜欢在乡下漫步。
  ✎ There’s plenty to discover as you <u>ramble</u> around this little island. 当漫步在这个小岛上时，有很多东西值得你去发现。
  **go for a ramble** 出去逛一逛（**go for a walk** 出去散步）
  ✎ I quite like the idea of <u>going for a ramble</u> one weekend. 我很喜欢一个周末去散散步的想法。
  **rambler** n. 漫步者
  ✎ Exploring really deep caves is not a task for the Sunday afternoon <u>rambler</u>.（L42）
+ **sentimentally** ad. 情感上，多情地 **<span id="⚓sentimentally">（🪐）</span>**
  **sentimental**
  + a1. 情感的（而非理智的） relating to emotions instead of reason
    **for sentimental reasons** 出于情感，出于感情方面的原因
    ✎ He wasn’t the sort of person who kept things <u>for sentimental reasons</u>. 他不是那种会因为感情原因而保留东西的人。
    **sentimental value** 情感方面的价值
    ✎ The rings that were stolen were of great <u>sentimental value</u>. 被盗的戒指具有极高的情感价值。
    **have a sentimental attachment to……** 在感情上对……有依恋
    ✎ He <u>had a sentimental attachment to</u> his birth-place. 他对自己的出生地有着浓浓的依恋。
  + a2. 煽情的 making people experience feelings of sadness, sympathy, love, etc., especially in a deliberate and obvious way
    ✎ a <u>sentimental</u> <u>song/ book/ movie</u> 煽情的歌曲/书/电影
  + a3. 多愁善感的（略贬义） expressing feelings of sadness, sympathy, love etc., especially in a way that seems inappropriate
    ✎ I’m just a <u>sentimental</u> old man. 我只是个多愁善感的老人。
  + **sentimentally** ad. 感情方面地，非理智地；多愁善感地；煽情地
    **be sentimentally attached to……** 在感情上对……有依恋
    ✎ The couple <u>are sentimentally attached to</u> each other. 这对夫妇在感情上对彼此依依不舍/如胶似漆。（指人）
    ✎ She <u>was sentimentally attached to</u> this house, for even though it was far too big for her needs, she persisted in living there long after her husband’s death.（本文-指物）
+ **preside** v. ① 主持（会议等）；② 掌管，领导
  **preside at……** 主持……
  ✎ I shall be pleased to <u>preside at</u> your meetings. 我很乐意主持你们的会议。
  ✎ They asked if I would <u>preside at</u> the committee meeting. 他们问我是否愿意主持委员会会议。
  **preside over……** 掌管，领导
  ✎ The city council is <u>presided over</u> by the mayor. 市议会由市长领导。（被动）
  ✎ Finch <u>presided over</u> the company for 30 years. 芬奇掌管这家公司30年。（主动）
  ✎ Aunt Harriet <u>presided over</u> an invisible army of servants that continuously scrubbed, cleaned, and polished.（本文）
  + 词根：**sid/ sed**: sit 坐（L47）
    表头1 | 表头2 | 表头3 | 表头3 |
    ---- | ---- | ---- | ---- 
    pre<u>sid</u>e | 主持；掌管（**pre-**：先） | <u>sed</u>ate | 镇静的，安静的 
    pre<u>sid</u>ent | 总统；经理；大学校长 | <u>sed</u>ative | 镇静剂
    pre<u>sid</u>ency | 主席/总统的职位(或任期等) | <u>sed</u>iment | 沉淀物
    re<u>sid</u>e | 居住 | <u>sed</u>ulous | 勤劳的，勤奋的（多指脑力工作者）
    re<u>sid</u>ent | 居民 | as<u>sid</u>uous | 勤劳的，勤奋的（多指脑力工作者）
    re<u>sid</u>ence | 住宅 | in<u>sid</u>ious | 潜伏的，潜藏的
    con<u>sid</u>er | 考虑 | sub<u>sid</u>e | v. 平息
    con<u>sid</u>erate | 体谅的；为(他人)着想的 | sub<u>sid</u>y | 补助金，津贴
    con<u>sid</u>eration | 考虑 | sub<u>sid</u>iary | 辅助的；次要的
  
    ✎ However, there is an even more <u>insidious</u> kind of pollution that particularly affects urban areas and invades our daily lives, and that is noise.（L47）
    ✎ An all-night party on New Year’s Eve provided me with a good excuse for not carrying out either of these new resolutions on the first day of the year, but on the second, I applied myself <u>assiduously</u> to the task.（L50）
    ✎ I wanna hold you till I die, till we both break down and cry. I wanna hold you till the fear in me <u>subsides</u>.（**break down and cry** 抑制不住感情而哭了出来（习语））（Rod Stewart《Sometimes When We Touch》）
+ **unrelenting** a. 不屈不挠的；持续不断的
  + a1. 非常坚决的，不屈不挠的 extremely determined, never weakening in effort or admitting defeat
    ✎ He was <u>unrelenting</u> in his search for the truth about his father. 他坚持不懈地寻找关于父亲的真相。
    ✎ She will be remembered as an <u>unrelenting</u> opponent of racial discrimination. 作为一个种族歧视的坚定反对者，她将被人们铭记。
  + a2.（不愉快的事）持续不断的 an unpleasant situation that is unrelenting continues for a long time without stopping 
    ✎ an <u>unrelenting</u> downpour of rain 持续不断的倾盆大雨
    ✎ the <u>unrelenting</u> pressures of the job 工作中的持续的压力
  同义词：
  **relentless**
  ✎ her <u>relentless</u> pursuit of perfection 她对完美的不懈追求
  ✎ a regime that was <u>relentless</u> in its persecution of dissidents 一个不屈不挠的迫害不同政见者的政权
  ✎ the <u>relentless</u> crying of a small baby 小婴儿没完没了的哭声
  ✎ a family facing <u>relentless</u> financial problems 一个面临持续财务问题的家庭
  词族：
  **relent** v. 态度缓和；强度减弱
  ✎ At last her father <u>relented</u> and came to visit her. 最终，她的父亲态度缓和了，前来探望她。
  ✎ The pressure on us to finish this task will not <u>relent</u>. 我们（肩负的）完成这项任务的压力将不会减弱。
  近义词：
  **incessant** a.（贬义）（指事情）持续不断的，没完没了的（L47） (usually disapproving) never stopping
  词根 **ces**：停止
  ✎ <u>incessant</u> <u>noise/ rain/ chatter</u> 没完没了的噪音/雨/唠叨
  ✎ A recent survey of the effects of noise revealed (surprisingly?) that dogs barking <u>incessantly</u> in the night rated the highest form of noise pollution on a scale ranging from 1 to 7.（L47）
  **perpetual, eternal, everlasting** a. 永恒的，长久的；没完没了的（L45）
  **insistent** a. 声音持续不断的；坚持要求的（L42）
  **persistent** a. 坚持不懈的；没完没了的（L42）
+ **disillusion** v. 使幻想破灭
  英文释义：to make someone realize that something which they thought was true or good is not really true or good
  ✎ I hate to <u>disillusion</u> you, but not everyone is as honest as you. 我不愿意打击你，但并不是每个人都像你一样诚实。
  **be disillusioned <u>with/ by</u>……** 对……大失所望
  ✎ Voters <u>are disillusioned with/ by</u> the democratic process. 选民对民主进程感到失望。
  **be disenchanted with……** 对……大失所望（**disenchant** 使幻想破灭）
  ✎ After three divorces he <u>became disenchanted with</u> married life. 离婚三次后，他对婚姻生活不再抱有幻想/大失所望。
  以上表达意为在认清事实之后，发现不像原来想象得美好，所以大失所望
  以下表达单纯指对某事失望
  **be disappointed <u>with/ by/ at</u>……** 对某事很失望
  **feel let down** 感到很失望
  **let sb. down** 让某人很失望
  ✎ Hey, Jude! Don’t <u>let me down</u>. You have found her, now go and get her. Remember to let her into your heart. Then you can start to make it better.（The Beatles《Hey Jude》）
+ **qualification** n. 资格，能力；文凭，资质证书
  + n1.（某工作需要的）资格，能力 an ability or quality that you need in order to do a particular job or position
    **qualification for……**
    ✎ Previous teaching experience is a necessary <u>qualification for</u> this job. 以前的教学经验是这份工作的必要资质。
    **qualification to do sth.** 做某事的资格/能力
    ✎ There have been questions about his <u>qualifications to</u> lead the company. 关于他领导公司的能力存在疑问。
    ✎ Does he have the right <u>qualifications to</u> become a Supreme Court Justice? 他有资格成为最高法院法官吗？
  + n2. 文凭，资质证书 an official record showing that you have finished a training course or have the necessary skills, etc.
    ✎ <u>academic/ vocational</u> <u>qualifications</u> 学术/职业证书
    ✎ You’ll never get a good job if you don’t have any <u>qualifications</u>. 如果你没有任何文凭，你永远找不到好工作。
  + **qualify** v.（使）有资格或能力
    **qualify as** 有……的能力
    ✎ He <u>qualified as</u> a doctor last year. 他去年取得了医生资质。
    **qualify sb. to do sth.** 使某人有能力/有资格做某事
    ✎ The test <u>qualifies</u> you <u>to</u> drive heavy vehicles. 这次考试使你有资格驾驶重型车辆。
    **qualify sb. for sth.** 使某人有资格获得某物
    ✎ This training course will <u>qualify</u> you <u>for</u> a better job. 这门培训课程将使你有资格获得更好的工作。
    ✎ Membership <u>qualifies</u> you <u>for</u> a discount on purchases. 会员身份使您有资格享受购物折扣。


### 🕹️ **课文讲解**
+ **It is a good thing (that)……** 幸亏……（固定搭配）
  ✎ <u>It is a good thing that</u> we brought an umbrella. 幸亏我们带伞了。
+ “if”型的虚拟语气复习（L17）
  **与现在事实相反：**
  **If + S. + <u>did/ were</u>, S. + <u>would/ should/ could/ might</u> + do**
+ **air** v. 公开表达…… to express your opinions publicly
  **air one’s <u>views/ opinions/ grievances/ complaints</u> (on……)** 表达某人（对……）的观点/看法/委屈/抱怨
  ✎ In an interview, the singer <u>aired his views on</u> family life. 在一次采访中，这位歌手表达了他对家庭生活的看法。
> 仿写第1句
  在会上每个人都将有机会(get a chance)当前的局势发表看法。
  At the meeting everyone will get a chance to <u>air their views on</u> the current situation.
+ **topic** 话题
  **a topic of** <u>conversation/ discussion/ debate</u> 一个交谈的/讨论的/辩论的话题
  **a** <u>sensitive/ controversial</u> **topic** 一个敏感的/人争议的话题
+ **servant**
  domestic servant 家仆
  maidservant 女仆，女佣（L36）
  public servant（政府的）公务员，公仆
  civil servant （政府的）文职人员
  ✎ Readers happily accepted the fact that an obscure <u>maidservant</u> was really the hero’s mother.（L36）
  ✎ The Swedes were the first to recognize that public officials like <u>civil servants</u>, police officers, health inspectors or tax-collectors can make mistakes or act over-zealously in the belief that they are serving the public.（L53）
+ **leisurely** a.&ad. 悠闲的/地，从容的/地 done without hurrying
  ✎ a <u>leisurely</u> <u>bath/ meal/ stroll</u> 一个悠闲的洗澡/吃饭/散步
  ✎ Couples strolled <u>leisurely</u> along the beach. 成双成对的情侣沿着海滩悠然漫步。
+ do (the) housework = do (the) household chores 做家务（L13）
  <u>do/ wash</u> the dishes = do the washing-up 洗碗 (习语)
  do the <u>laundry/ washing</u> 洗衣服（laundry [U]）
+ **attach sth. to sth.** 把某物和某物固定在一块
  ✎ The sides of the dish were so smooth that it was almost impossible to <u>attach</u> hawsers and chains <u>to</u> the rim without damaging it.（L43）
  **be attached to <u>sb./ sth.</u>** 依恋……，（感情上）固定在一块（被动）
  英文释义：to like someone or something very much, because you have known them or had them for a long time
  ✎ I’ve never seen two people so <u>attached to</u> each other. 我从未见过两个人如此依恋。
  ⬇ 加副词修饰
  ✎ The children <u>are very attached to</u> their grandparents. 孩子们非常依恋他们的祖父母。
  ✎ We’ve <u>grown deeply attached to</u> this house and would hate to move. 我们变得深深地依恋这所房子，不想搬走。
  ✎ I <u>am sentimentally attached to</u> my old guitar. 我在感情上很依恋我的旧吉他。
+ **<u>much/ far</u> too……** 实在是太……（much, far加强语气）
  ✎ Alice is <u>far too</u> young to get married. 在结婚这件事上，爱丽丝实在太小了。
  **<u>slightly/ a little/ a bit/ a little bit</u> too……** 有点太……
  ✎ I think you’re <u>a bit too</u> young to watch this. 我觉得你有点太小了，不能看这个。
+ **persist**
  + v1. 坚持，执意 to continue to do sth. in spite of difficulties or opposition, in a way that can seem unreasonable
    **persist in……** 坚持/执意……
    ✎ Why do you <u>persist in</u> blaming yourself for what happened? 你何必执意因为这件事自责呢？
    ✎ She <u>persisted in</u> her search for the truth. 她坚持寻求真相。
  + v2.（坏事）持续（存在或发生）if sth. bad persists, it continues to exist or happen
    ✎ If the pain <u>persists</u>, you must see a doctor. 如果疼痛持续，你必须去看医生。
    ✎ Competition between ourselves, person against person, community against community, still <u>persists</u>, however; and it is as fierce as it ever was.（B4L45）
  + **persistent** a. 坚持的，执意的；（坏事）没完没了的
    ✎ She can be very <u>persistent</u> when she wants something. 当她想要什么的时候，她会非常执着。
    ✎ a <u>persistent</u> cough 持续咳嗽
    ✎ He resigned over <u>persistent</u> rumours of his affair with an actress. 他因与一位女演员有染的没完没了的谣言而辞职。
+ ┏ **long after……** 在……之后很久（L43）
  ┗ **long before……** 在……之前很久
  ┏ **shortly after……** 在……之后不久
  ┗ **shortly before……**  在……之前不久
  **shortly afterwards** 不久之后
+ **entertain** v.（在家中）宴客 to invite people to eat or drink with you as your guests, especially in your home
  ✎ I don’t <u>entertain</u> very often. 我不常请客。（不及物）
  ✎ Bob and Liz <u>entertained</u> us to dinner last night. 鲍勃和丽兹昨晚请我们吃饭。（及物）
+ **lavish** a. 慷慨的，大方的 very generous
  **entertain lavishly** 大宴宾客
  ✎ The Bradfords always <u>entertained lavishly</u> at Christmas. 布拉德福德一家总是在圣诞节大宴宾客。
+ **immaculate = spotless** a. 一尘不染的 very clean and tidy
+ parquet n.[U] 镶木地板 small flat blocks of wood fitted together in a pattern that cover the floor of  a room
  ✎ a <u>parquet</u> floor 一块镶木地板
+ **silver = silverware** n. 银器，银餐具 spoons, forks, dishes etc that are made of silver
  ✎ It was my job to polish the <u>silver</u>. 擦亮银器是我的工作。
+ **gleam** v. 发出柔和的光 shine softly
  ✎ He had polished the table-top until it <u>gleamed</u>. 他把桌面擦到闪闪发光。
  ✎ <u>gleaming</u> windows 闪闪发光的窗户
  ✎ his <u>gleaming</u> white teeth 他闪闪发光的白牙
+ **cabinet** n. 储藏柜 piece of furniture with drawers or shelves for storing or displaying things
+ **miraculous** a. 奇迹般的 like a miracle; completely unexpected and very lucky
  ✎ A teenage boy had a <u>miraculous</u> escape from death last night when he fell into an ice-cold river. 昨晚，一个十几岁的男孩掉进了一条冰冷的河里，奇迹般地逃脱了死亡。
  **miraculously** ad. 奇迹般地
  ✎ They <u>miraculously</u> survived the plane crash. 他们奇迹般地在飞机失事中幸存了下来。
+ **preside over……** 掌管……
  ✎ He <u>presided over</u> the company for 10 years. 他掌管公司已10年之久。
  ✎ Some people believe the Fates <u>preside over</u> man’s destiny. 有些人认为命运女神掌管着人类的命运。
+ **army** n. a large number of people who are doing the same thing or in the same situation
  **army of……** ……的大军
  ✎ <u>Armies of</u> rescue workers are sorting through the rubble. 大批救援人员正在废墟中寻找。（**rubble** 碎砖碎石）
  ✎ the <u>army of</u> the unemployed 失业大军
+ **scrub** v. 彻底擦洗某物 clean sth. thoroughly by rubbing hard, esp. with a brush and soap and water
+ “把A称为B”的表达（复制自L4）
  **refer to A as B**
  **call A B**
  **address A as B**
  **know A as B**
+ **shifting** a. 不停变化或移动的 always changing or moving
+ **…… with such frequency that……**
  ┏ …… with such frequency that……（原文-用名词更正式）
  ┗ …… so frequently that……（同义表达）
> 仿写第1段倒数第3句后半部分（with such n. that）
  电话铃如此频繁地响起以至于我甚至没机会睡觉。
  The telephone rang <u>with such frequency that</u> I didn’t even get a chance to sleep.
  他如此轻松地通过了考试以至于老师怀疑(suspect sb. of doing)他作了弊
  He passed the exam <u>with such ease that</u> the teacher suspected him of cheating.
  他上楼如此之艰难以至于我还以为(be under the impression that……)他腿受伤了。
  He walked up the stairs <u>with such difficulty that</u> we were under the impression that he had injured his leg.
+ **learn (of/ about) sth.** 获悉，得知 to become aware of sth. by hearing about it from sb. else
  ✎ I <u>learnt of</u> her arrival from a close friend. 我从一位好朋友那里听说了她的到来。
  ✎ How did they react when they <u>learned</u> the news? 当他们得知这个消息时，他们的反应如何？
+ **in those days** 在当年
  **these days** 当今，现如今（L4）
+ **enlightened** a. 开明的 someone with enlightened attitudes has sensible, modern views and treats people fairly and kindly
  ✎ an <u>enlightened</u> <u>policy/ attitude/……</u> 开明的政策/态度……
+ **<u>domestic/ medical/ nursing/ teaching/ engineering/ administrative</u> staff**
  家里的全体佣人/一所医院的全体医护人员/全体护士/全体老师/全体工程技术人员/全体管理人员
+ **“a. + to do” 通常用主动**（L13）
  ┏ she was extremely difficult to please（原文）
  ┗ to please her was extremely difficult（同义表达）
+ **fickle** a. 反复无常的，多变的 often changing
  ✎ a <u>fickle</u> lover 一个花心情人
  ✎ the <u>fickle</u> finger of fate 命运的无常（固定搭配-首韵）
  **fickleness** n.反复无常，多变
  ✎ the <u>fickleness</u> of businessmen and politicians 商人和政客的反复无常
  ✎ the <u>fickleness</u> of the English climate 英国气候的多变
+ **carry on sth.** 持续做某事，一直做某事 to continue doing, pursuing, or operating
  ✎ We have <u>carried on</u> a correspondence for years. 我们已经通信多年了。
  ✎ He <u>carried on</u> his baking business until he retired. 直到退休，他一直经营烘焙生意。
+ **unrelenting** a. 非常坚决的，不屈不挠的
+ **be disillusioned <u>with/ by</u>……**  对……大失所望/幻想破灭
  ⬇ 加副词修饰
  **be** <u>very/ extremely/ completely/ utterly/ increasingly/ sadly</u> **disillusioned <u>with/ by</u>……**
  ✎ As she grew older, Laura <u>became increasingly disillusioned with</u> politics. 随着年龄的增长，劳拉对政治越来越失望。
  ✎ I <u>feel utterly disillusioned by</u> his refusal to take any action. 他拒绝采取任何行动，我为此感到彻底失望。
+ **charge**
  **be in charge of……** 管理/主管/掌管……（L1）
  **be <u>in the charge of……/ in one’s charge</u>** 由……管理
  **take charge of……** 接管……
  **put sb. in charge of……** 交给某人管理……
  ┏ Peter is <u>in charge of</u> the company. 彼得管理这家公司。
  ┗ The company is <u>in the charge of Peter/ in his charge</u>. 这家公司归彼得管理。
  ┗ Peter will be <u>taking charge of</u> the company next Monday. 彼得将在下周一接管这家公司。
  ┗ They <u>put</u> Peter <u>in charge of</u> the company. 他们让彼得来管理公司。
  ┗ Peter <u>was put in charge of</u> the company. 彼得被指派管理这家公司。
+ **无法描述**
◇ I **cannot find words to describe** the beauty of the West Lake. 我无法用言语形容西湖的美丽。
◇ The beauty of the West Lake **is beyond <u>words/ description</u>**. 西湖的美丽难以形容。
◇ The beauty of the West Lake **defies description**. 西湖的美丽无法描述。（**defy** v. 使……不可能）
◇ The beauty of the West Lake **is more than words can describe**. 西湖的美丽是语言无法描述的。
+ **industrious** a. 勤劳的
  **industriousness** n. 勤奋
  形近词：
  **industrial** a. 工业的
  ✎ the <u>industrious</u> ant 勤劳的蚂蚁
  ✎ the <u>industrial</u> revolution 工业革命
+ ┏ **in addition to……**
  ┏ **besides……**
  ┏ **as well as……**
  ┏ **<u>apart from……/ aside from……</u>**
  ┗ 除了……之外还有（包含）
  ✎ <u>Apart from</u> an interesting-looking carved dagger, the box was full of crockery, much of it broken.（L34）
  ✎ There they collected women <u>as well as</u> food and drink, and a life of ease had made them soft.（B4L9）
  ┏ **<u>except……/ except for……</u>**
  ┏ **excluding……**
  ┏ **but……**
  ┏ **other than……**
  ┏ **with the exception of……**（L27）
  ┏ **<u>apart from……/ aside from……</u>**
  ┗ 排除……之外有（排除）
  ✎ Yet, in real life, circumstances do sometimes conspire to bring about coincidences which anyone <u>but</u> a nineteenth century novelist would find incredible.（L36）
  ┏ **<u>what is more/ what’s more</u>**
  ┏ **moreover/ furthermore**
  ┏ **besides** ad.
  ┏ **in addition**
  ┏ **additionally**
  ┗ 此外，而且，还（表递进）
  ✎ He could not find his fifty pence piece anywhere, and <u>what is more</u>, he could no get his arm out.（L15）
+ **expert** a. 熟练的，专家水平的 showing special skill or knowledge
  ✎ an <u>expert</u> <u>gardener/ driver</u> 一个专业的园丁/司机（作定语）
  **be expert <u>in/ at</u>……** 在……方面很专业（作表语）
  ┏ Bessie was an <u>expert</u> cook.（原文）
  ┗ Bessie <u>was expert in/ at</u> cooking.（同义表达）
+ **<u>play/ perform/ act</u> +  (the <u>role/ part</u> of)……** 扮演……的角色（L22）
  ✎ He <u>played/ performed/ acted (the role/ part of)</u> Othello. 她扮演奥赛罗这个角色。
  **play a…… <u>role/ part</u> in……** 在……方面发挥……的作用
  ✎ The river which forms the eastern boundary of our farm has always <u>played an important part in</u> our lives.（L56）
  ✎ Not all sounds made by animals serve as language, and we have only to turn to that extraordinary discovery of echo-location in bats to see a case <u>in</u> which the voice <u>plays a strictly utilitarian role</u>.（B4L7）
+ before的译法（L2）
  **强调主句的时间很长时，译为“才”**
  ✎ It will be a long time before we meet again. 要过很久我们才能见面。
  ✎ Looking at his watch, he saw that it was one o’clock, but the bell struck thirteen times <u>before</u> it stopped. 才（L2）
  **强调主句的时间很短时，译为“就”**
  ✎ I hadn’t waited long before he came. 我没等多久他就来了。
  **然后**
  ✎ I shaved <u>before</u> I went to the party. 我刮了胡子然后去参加了聚会。
  ✎ Alfred stayed in the camp a week <u>before</u> he returned to Athelney.（B4L9）
+ **weakness**（L26）
  1. n. [U] 懦弱，软弱
    ✎ So let us begin anew —— remembering on both sides that civility is not <u>a sign of weakness</u>, and sincerity is always subject to proof. Let us never negotiate out of fear, but let us never fear to negotiate.（John F.Kennedy就职演说）
  2. n. [C] 弱点，缺点
    ✎ In their efforts to persuade us to buy this or that product, advertisers have made a close study of human nature and have classified all our little <u>weaknesses</u>.（L26）
    + 反义词：
      **strength** n. [U] 力量；[C] 优点，长处
      **strength and weakness** 优缺点
      ✎ For we know that our patchwork heritage is <u>a strength</u>, not <u>a weakness</u>. We are a nation of Christians and Muslims, Jews and Hindus, and nonbelievers.
      因为我们知道，我们打补丁的文化遗产是一种优势，而不是劣势。我们是一个由基督徒、穆斯林、犹太人、印度教徒和无宗教信仰者组成的国家。（奥巴马就职演说）
+ **be absent from……** 不在……
+ **party** n. 一群；一队；一组（L8）
  ✎ a <u>search/ rescue</u> <u>party</u> 一支搜寻队/一支救援队
  ✎ a <u>party</u> of <u>tourists/ sightseers</u> 一群游客/观光客
  ✎ The only regular visitors to the monastery in winter are <u>parties</u> of skiers who go there at Christmas and Easter.（L8）
+ **<u>prepare/ cook/ fix</u> dinner** 做晚饭（fix 为口语表达，表示简单凑活一顿）
+ ┏ **not only…… but……**
  ┏ **not only…… but also……**
  ┏ **not only…… but…… <u>as well/ too</u>**
  ┏ **not only…… <u>as well/ too</u>**
  ┏ **not only……**
  ┗ 不但……而且……
  注：not only放句首，后面一定要倒装。
  ✎ <u>Not only</u> **had** the poor man been arrested, <u>but</u> he had been sent to prison <u>as well</u>.（L5）
+ **well** ad. 相当地，颇为，……得多 a lot, or to a great degree
  **well <u>before/ after/ over/ above/ below/ worth</u>……**
  ✎ I don’t know how old he is, but he looks <u>well over</u> forty. 我不知道他多大，但他看起来恐怕远远超过四十岁了。
  ✎ Pete left the party <u>well before</u> you got there. 皮特在你到达之前很久就离开了聚会。
  ✎ The castle is <u>well worth</u> a visit. 这座城堡非常值得一游。
+ **<u>above/ below</u> (the) standard** 高于/低于标准
  ✎ Your work is <u>above/ below (the) standard</u>. 你的工作高于/低于正常水平。
+ **<u>bump/ run</u> into** （**bump** 碰，撞（拟声词））
  ① 撞到……上
  ✎ The car <u>bumped/ ran into</u> a big pine. 汽车撞上了一棵大松树。
  ② 偶遇/邂逅……
  ✎ I happened to <u>bump/ run into</u> a friend of mine in the street. 我在街上碰巧偶遇了我的一个朋友。
+ **mumble** v. 小声咕哝 to say something too quietly or not clearly enough, so that people cannot hear what is said
  ✎ He was still <u>mumbling</u> something about hospitals at the end of the party when he slipped on a piece of ice and broke his left leg.（L29）
+ **<u>trip/ stumble</u> <u>over/ on</u> sth.** 在……上绊倒
  ✎ He <u>tripped/ stumbled over/ on</u> a rock. 他被一块石头绊倒了。
+ **flying** 飞也似地
  ✎ Chairs and tables <u>went flying</u> into the arcade.（L6）
+ **narrowly miss** 勉强躲过/险些撞上
  ✎ The *Titanic* turned just in time, <u>narrowly missing</u> the immense wall of ice which rose over 100 feet out of the water beside her.（L10）
+ **mirth** n.[U] (fml.) 欢笑 happiness and laughter
  ◇ Her body began to **shake with mirth**. 她的身体开始笑得花枝乱颤。
  ◇ The performance **produced much mirth among** the audience. 这场演出使得观众们非常开心。
  ◇ That **caused considerable mirth amongst** pupils. 这引起了这些小学生一阵哄堂大笑。
+ **<u>draw/ come to/ arrive at/ reach</u> a conclusion** 得出结论
  **bring…… to a conclusion** 使……结末
  ✎ In the nineteenth century, a novelist would <u>bring</u> his story <u>to a conclusion</u> by presenting his readers with a series of coincidences — most of them wildly improbable.（L36）
+ **catastrophe** 大灾难
  ✎ The telephone rings and this marks the prelude to an unforeseen series of <u>catastrophes</u>.（L33）
+ **have a <u>difficult/ hard</u> time doing** 做某事很困难（L43）
+ **…… of all shapes and sizes** 各种形状和尺寸的……
  ✎ Before long, biscuits <u>of all shapes and sizes</u> began arriving at the factory.（L26）
  **…… of all kinds** 各种各样的……
  ✎ …… , vehicles <u>of all kinds</u>, especially large container trucks thundering through quiet village, ……（L47）
+ **find one’s way** （某物）到达……；（某人）找到……的路
  ✎ Very few of the fifty pence pieces and pound coins I have given him have <u>found their way</u> there.（L15）

---

## **Lesson 50 - New Year resolutions**
### **课文原文** [🌏](#第三册目录)
<font color=gray size=4>The New Year is a time for resolutions. Mentally, at least, most of us could compile formidable lists of ‘dos’ and ‘don’ts’. The same old favourites recur year in year out with monotonous regularity. We resolve to get up earlier each morning, eat less, find more time to play with the children, do a thousand and one jobs about the house, be nice to people we don’t like, drive carefully, and take the dog for a walk every day. Past experience has taught us that certain accomplishments are beyond attainment. If we remain inveterate smokers, it is only because we have so often experienced the frustration that results from failure. Most of us fail in our efforts at self-improvement because our schemes are too ambitious and we never have time to carry them out. We also make the fundamental error of announcing our resolutions to everybody so that we look even more foolish when we slip back into our bad old ways. Aware of these pitfalls, this year I attempted to keep my resolutions to myself. I limited myself to two modest ambitions: to do physical exercise every morning and to read more of an evening. An all-night party on New Year’s Eve provided me with a good excuse for not carrying out either of these new resolutions on the first day of the year, but on the second, I applied myself assiduously to the task.

The daily exercises lasted only eleven minutes and I proposed to do them early in the morning before anyone had got up. The self-discipline required to drag myself out of bed eleven minutes earlier than usual was considerable. Nevertheless, I managed to creep down into the living room for two days before anyone found me out. After jumping about on the carpet and twisting the human frame into uncomfortable positions, I sat down at the breakfast table in an exhausted condition. It was this that betrayed me. The next morning the whole family trooped in to watch the performance. That was really unsettling, but I fended off the taunts and jibes of the family good-humouredly and soon everybody got used to the idea. However, my enthusiasm waned. The time I spent at exercises gradually diminished. Little by little the eleven minutes fell to zero. By January 10th, I was back to where I had started from. I argued that if I spent less time exhausting myself at exercises in the morning, I would keep my mind fresh for reading when I got home from work. Resisting the hypnotizing effect of television, I sat in my room for a few evenings with my eyes glued to a book. One night, however, feeling cold and lonely, I went downstairs and sat in front of the television pretending to read. That proved to be my undoing, for I soon got back to my old bad habit of dozing off in front of the screen. I still haven’t given up my resolution to do more reading. In fact, I have just bought a book entitled *How to Read a Thousand Words a Minute*. Perhaps it will solve my problem, but I just haven’t had time to read it!</font>


### 🌻 **单词讲解**
+ **formidable, awesome** a. 令人望而生畏的
  ✎ <u>a/ an</u> <u>formidable/ awesome</u> <u>task/ challenge</u> 一个令人望而生畏的任务/挑战
  形近词：
  **forbidding** a. 不友好的，冷冰冰的（L36）
  ✎ a <u>forbidding</u> <u>place/ appearance</u> 一个不友好的地方/一副拒人于千里之外的模样
+ **recur** v. 再次发生；反复发生
  ✎ We must make sure that the problem does not <u>recur</u>. 我们必须确保这个问题不再发生。
  ✎ a <u>recurring</u> <u>illness/ nightmare</u> 反复发作的疾病/多次出现的噩梦
  形近词：
  **occur** v. 发生（意料之外，比happen更正式）
  ✎ When exactly did the incident <u>occur</u>? 这起事件究竟是什么时候发生的？
  ✎ Something unexpected <u>occurred</u>. 一个意想不到的事情发生了。
  **concur** v. 同意；同时发生
  ✎ We strongly <u>concur</u> <u>with</u> the recommendations of this report. 我们强烈赞同这份报告中提出的建议。（比agree with更正式）
  ✎ Everything <u>concurred</u> to produce the desired effect. 每件事都同时发生，产生了期望的效果。
  **incur** v. 招致，引起，带来（不好的结果）
  ✎ She had <u>incurred</u> the wrath of her father by marrying without his consent. 她未经父亲同意就结婚了，这引起了他父亲的愤怒。
+ **inveterate** a. 根深蒂固的，积习难改的（多贬义，指人、指事物都可）
  ✎ an <u>inveterate</u> <u>smoker/ drinker/ gambler/ liar</u> 一个老烟鬼/老酒鬼/赌棍/撒谎成性的人（指人）
  ✎ If we remain <u>inveterate</u> smokers, it is only because we have so often experienced the frustration that results from failure.（本文-指人）
  ✎ <u>inveterate</u> <u>hatred/ prejudice/ distrust</u> 根深蒂固的仇恨/偏见/不信任（指事物）
  ✎ Hatred is <u>inveterate</u> anger. — M.T.Cicero
  仇恨是根深蒂固的愤怒。 — 西塞罗
  **deep-seated/ deep-rooted** 根深蒂固的（中性，通常指事物）
  ✎ a <u>deep-seated/ deep-rooted</u> <u>bad habit/ faith in god</u> 一个根深蒂固的坏习惯/坚定的对上帝的信仰
  **die hard** 积习难改
  ✎ Old habits <u>die hard</u>. 积习难改。（谚语）
+ **assiduously** ad. 刻苦地
  **assiduous** a. 刻苦的（多指伏案的脑力工作）
  ✎ an <u>assiduous</u> <u>student/ researcher</u> 一个勤奋的学生/研究员
  + 词根：**sid/ sed**: sit 坐（L47、49）
    ✎ However, there is an even more <u>insidious</u> kind of pollution that particularly affects urban areas and invades our daily lives, and that is noise.（L47）
    ✎ Aunt Harriet <u>presided</u> <u>over</u> an invisible army of servants that continuously scrubbed, cleaned, and polished.（L49）
+ **betray** v. （人）背叛；（事物）无意中暴露
  v1. 背叛
  ✎ Judas <u>betrayed</u> Jesus. 犹大背叛了耶稣。
  **betray one’s <u>beliefs/ principles</u>** 背叛某人的信仰/原则
  v2. 无意中暴露
  ✎ Her voice <u>betrayed</u> her nervousness. 她的声音无意中暴露出了她的紧张。
  **betrayal** n.
  ✎ Forgetting history means <u>betrayal</u>. 忘记历史意味着背叛。
  近义表达：
  **cheat on sb.** 背叛（自己的伴侣）
  ✎ He <u>cheated on</u> his wife. 他背叛了他的老婆。
  **desert** 背叛（部队）
  ✎ As he hated army life, he decided to <u>desert</u> his regiment.（L30）
  **be <u>loyal/ disloyal</u> to……** 对……忠诚/不忠诚
  **betrayer, traitor, Judas** 叛徒
  ✎ You <u>Judas</u>！ 你这个叛徒！
+ **good-humo(u)redly** ad. 心情好地
  **good-humo(u)red** a. 心情好的
  **ill-humo(u)red** a. 心情不好的
  **humo(u)r = mood** 心情，情绪
  ✎ He is <u>in a good/ a bad/ an ill humor</u>. 他心情好/心情不好/心情不好。
  humo(u)r本义是指人的4种体液，古代西方人认为人的体液决定了性格、脾气，派生义表示人的心情。（4种体液与对应气质类型：blood-多血质, choler-胆汁质, phlegm-粘液质, melancholy-抑郁质**）


### 🕹️ **课文讲解**
+ **resolutions** 决心，决议，决定
  **New Year(’s) resolutions** 新年的决心
  ✎ ‘Have you made any <u>New Year’s resolutions</u>?’‘Yes, I’m going to eat more healthily and give up smoking.’
  ✎ **UN resolution** 联合国的决议

+ ┏ 到了该做某事的时候了
  ┗ **It’s time for sth.**
  ✎ <u>It’s time for</u> <u>school/ dinner/ bed</u>. 该上学/吃晚饭/睡觉了。（school/ dinner/ bed强调功能时，不加冠词）
  ┗ **It’s time to do sth.**
  ✎ <u>It’s time to</u> get up. 该起床了。
  ┗ **It’s (high/ about) time (that)……(虚拟)** 早该做某事了
  ✎ <u>It’s (high/ about) time (that)</u> we <u>went</u> home. 早该回家了。
  ✎ It’s already 5 o’clock now. Don’t you think it’s about time <u>we went home</u>?
  (A) we are going home; (B) we go home; (C) we went home; (D) we can go home（四级真题）
  ✎ If I were in movie, then it would be about time that I <u>buried</u> my head in my hands for a cry.
  (A) bury; (B) am burying; (C) buried; (D) would bury（2001考研真题）
+ **mentally**: at heart 在心中
+ **compile a list**: make a list（**compile** 编辑 (较文言)）
+ **dos and don’ts** 该做的事与不该做的事（名词短语）（助动词 → 名词）
  同变化的名词短语：
  **likes and dislikes** 喜欢做的事与不喜欢做的事（动词 → 名词）
  **ups and downs** （人生的）沉浮（副词 → 名词）
  **highs and lows** 兴衰（形容词&副词 → 名词）
  **ins and outs** 来龙去脉（介词&副词 → 名词）
+ **same old……** 司空见惯的，非常熟悉的（略贬）
  ✎ It’s the <u>same old</u> story. 还是那个老问题。
  ✎ It’s the <u>same old</u> excuse. 还是那个老借口。
  ✎ It’s the <u>same old</u> faces at the meeting. 会议上还是那些老面孔。
  ✎ ‘How are you doing?’‘<u>Same old</u>.’ 最近好吗？老样子。
+ **year in year out = year after year** 年复一年
  **day in day out = day after day** 日复一日
  **week in week out = week after week** 周复一周
  **month in month out = month after month** 月复一月
+ **with monotonous regularity** 老是，总是（固定搭配-贬义）（L44）
  ✎ The little boy wets the bed <u>with monotonous regularity</u>. 这个小男孩老是尿床。
  ✎ History repeats itself <u>with monotonous regularity</u>. 历史老是在重演。
> 仿写第3句
  这个老问题总是日复一日地重复出现。
  The same old story recurs day in day out with monotonous regularity.

+ ┏ 决定做某事
  ┗ **<u>resolve/ determine</u> to do……**（正式）
  ┗ **be <u>resolved/ determined</u> to do……**（正式）
  ┗ **decide to do……**（通俗）
  ┗ **make up one’s mind to do……**（通俗）
  ┗ **make a decision to do……**（通俗）
  ✎ I <u>determined to</u> lodge a complaint as soon as we arrived.（L37）
  **take the plunge** 长期考虑之后下定决心，豁出去
  ✎ If you have been thinking about buying shares, now could be the time to <u>take the plunge</u>. 如果你一直在考虑购买股票，现在可能是下决心去做的时候了。
+ **a <u>hundred/ thousand/ million</u> and one** = very many
+ **jobs about the house** 家务活（L13）
  **= housework** [U]
  **= household chores** [C]
  **do (the) <u>housework/ household chores</u>** 做家务
  ✎ I spent all morning <u>doing (the) housework/ household chores</u>.
  相关搭配：
  **do the <u> laundry/ washing</u>** 洗衣服
  **<u>do/ wash</u> the dishes = do the washing-up** 洗碗
  ✎ W: Have you asked your brother to <u>do the dishes</u>?
  M: Thousands of times.
  Q: What does the man mean?
  Answer: He has asked his brother to <u>wash the dishes</u> many times.
+ **take the dog for a walk** 遛狗（walk n.）
  **= walk the dog**（walk v.）
+ ┏ **every day** ad. 每天都
  ┗ **everyday** a. 日常的
+ **be beyond sth.** 无法……；不容……（L35）
  ✎ The car <u>is beyond repair</u>. 这辆汽车已经无法修理了。
  ✎ The rumor <u>is beyond belief</u>. 这个谣言是无法相信的。
  ✎ The situation <u>is beyond my control</u>. 这个局面是我无法控制的。
  ✎ The results <u>are beyond dispute/ controversy</u>.  这个结果是不容争辩的。
  ✎ Her beauty <u>is beyond words/ description</u>. 她的美丽是无法形容的。
  ✎ His conduct <u>is beyond reproach/ criticism</u>. 他的行为无可指摘。
  ✎ The pain <u>is beyond human endurance</u>. 这个疼痛是人无法忍受的。
  ✎ Working with you <u>is beyond my wildest dreams</u>. 和你一起工作是我梦寐以求的/做梦也想不到的。（wild 离奇的）
  ✎ We might say that justice has been done when a man’s innocence or guilt has been proved <u>beyond doubt</u>.（L35）
  **be beyond sb. = be a mystery to sb.** 是某人无法理解的（L41）
  ✎ Why people are prepared to tolerate a four-hour journey each day for the dubious privilege of living in the country <u>is beyond me</u>.（L41）
  ✎ It has always <u>been a mystery to me</u> why city dwellers, who appreciate all these things, obstinately pretend that they would prefer to live in the country.（L41）
+ an <u>inveterate</u> <u>smoker/ drinker/ gambler/ liar</u> 一个老烟鬼/老酒鬼/赌棍/撒谎成性的人
  old friend 老朋友
  regular, patron 老顾客，常客
  hardened smuggler 老牌走私犯（L11）
  maidservant 老妈子，女仆（L36）
+ 【✔】**it is because……** 这是因为……（主系表）
  【✔】**the reason is that……** 原因是……（表语从句）
  【✘】**The reason is because……**（重复）
  ┏ ……, it is only because……（原文）
  ┗ ……, the only reason is that……（同义表达）
+ **result from…… = be caused by……** 由……导致/带来
  **result in…… = cause……** 导致……
+ ┏ 失败
  ┗ **fail to do** 未能做成某事
  ┗ **fail in one’s <u>efforts/ attempts</u> <u>at sth./ to do sth.</u>** 努力/尝试做某事但没有成功（固定搭配-更文气）
  ✎ Latham试图驾机飞跃英吉利海峡，但没有成功。
  Latham <u>failed in his efforts/ attempts to</u> fly across the English Channel.
  ✎ 考古学家试图确认被修复的女神像的身份，但没有成功。
  The archaeologists <u>failed in their efforts/ attempts to</u> discover the identity of the reconstructed statue.
  The archaeologists <u>failed in their efforts/ attempts at</u> the identification of the reconstructed statue.（名词表达，更显正式）
+ **scheme** n. ① 计划，方案；② 阴谋诡计（L36）
  **schemes and intrigues** 阴谋诡计
+ ┏ **get <u>round/ around</u> to <u>sth. /doing sth.</u>** 有时间（找到时间）做某事（to作介词，后接名词或动名词）（round [英]；around [美]）（L46）
  ┗ **<u>never/ not</u> get <u>round/ around</u> to <u>sth./ doing</u>** 没时间做某事
  ✎ It had broken down the previous summer, and though I promised to repair it, I had <u>never got round to</u> it.（L46）
  ✎ W: I’m having trouble slicing the bread with this knife.（**slice** n. 薄薄的一片；v. 切成片）
  M: Oh. Sorry about that. I have<u>n’t gotten around to</u> sharpening it yet.
  Q: What can be inferred about the knife?
  Answer: It’s dull.（老托福听力片段）
+ **carry <u>sth. 🗘 out</u>** 执行，实施
  ✎ We <u>carried out</u> her instructions precisely. 我们精确地执行了她的指示。
+ **fundamental** a. 根本性的
  ✎ <u>fundamental</u> <u>error/ mistake</u> 根本性的错误
  ✎ <u>fundamental</u> <u>change/ difference</u>  根本性的改变/差别
  **make the fundamental error of doing sth.** 犯了……的根本性的错误
  ✎ 他犯了轻敌这个根本性的错误。
  He <u>made the fundamental error of</u> despising his enemy.
+ **so (that) 作连词时，通常来说有两种用法：**（L43）
  1. **引导结果状语从句**，译为“**所以、因此**”，从句谓语动词中通常没有情态动词。
  2. **引导目的状语从句**，译为“**以便于……，为了……**” = in order that……，从句谓语动词中通常会出现情态动词 can, could, may, might, should, would 等。
   
  ✎ Drive carefully <u>so that</u> everyone <u>can</u> enjoy a long life. 小心驾驶，以便大家都能长寿。（目的）
  ✎ It had been purchased by a local authority <u>so that</u> an enormous pie <u>could</u> be baked for an annual fair.（L43-目的）
  ✎ In the new country he became absorbed in making a new life for the two of us, <u>so that</u> he gradually ceased to grieve.（L57-结果）
+ **slip** 滑，滑倒，滑落（意外情况下）
  ✎ He was still mumbling something about hospitals at the end of the party when he <u>slipped</u> on a piece of ice and broke his left leg.（L29）
  **slip into……** 渐渐陷入某种不良状态或处境 to gradually start to be in a bad state or situation
  ✎ <u>slip into</u> <u>debt/ unconsciousness/ ……</u> 渐渐陷入债务中/昏迷状态……
  ✎ He had begun to <u>slip into</u> debt. 他开始慢地陷入债务中。
  ✎ She <u>slipped into</u> unconsciousness and died the next day. 她慢慢陷入了昏迷状态，第二天就死了。
  ✎ The country is <u>slipping into</u> recession. 这个国家正在慢慢陷入萧条。
+ **pitfall** n. 陷阱；易犯的错误，易出现的问题 a likely mistake or problem in a situation
  ✎ the potential <u>pitfalls</u> of buying a house 买房的潜在的容易犯的错误
  ✎ Her advice helped me avoid some of the common <u>pitfalls</u>. 她的建议帮助我避免了一些常见的错误。
  **keep sth. to oneself = keep sth. secret** 保密
  ✎ I <u>keep</u> my love for Helen <u>to myself</u>. 我把对海伦的爱藏在心里。
  **keep sth. from sb.** 向某人保密某事
  ┏ The only other people who knew the secret were Joe and Bob. They did <u>not</u> even <u>tell</u> their wives.（L30）
  ┗ They even <u>kept</u> it <u>from</u> their wives.（同义表达）
  **reveal a secret** 揭示秘密（L24）
  **a secret becomes known** 秘密被公开
+ **modest** a. 谦虚的，谦逊的（指人）；适中的，适度的，不过分的（指事物）
+ **limit oneself to sth.** 给自己限定……
  ✎ I <u>limit myself to</u> 2 glasses of beer a day. 我限定自己每天只喝两杯啤酒。
  ✎ She <u>limits herself to</u> 1,000 kilocalories a day to lose weight. 她限制自己每天最多摄入1000大卡来减肥。
+ **do (physical) exercises** 锻炼身体
+ **of an evening [英] = in the evenings** 在晚上
  **of a weekend [英] = at weekends** 在周末
+ **on…… Eve** 在（某重要日期）前夜
+ ┏ **provide sb. with sth.** 为某人提供某物
  ┏ **an excuse for (doing) sth.** 做某事的借口
  ┗ **sth. provide sb. with a good excuse for (doing) sth.** 某事物给某人提供了一个做某事的好借口
  ✎ 突然得病使他有借口没有参加会议。
  A sudden illness <u>provided</u> him <u>with a good excuse for</u> not attending the meeting.
  ✎ 漫长辛苦的旅程使我有借口很早去睡觉。
  A long and arduous journey <u>provided</u> me <u>with a good excuse for</u> going to bed early.
  **plead** <u>ignorance/ illness/ a headache/ tiredness/ insanity</u> 以无知/得病/头疼/疲劳/精神失常为借口（L46）
+ ┏ **either of……** 两个中任何一个……
  ┗ **each of……** 三个以上中任何一个……
  ┏ **neither of……** 两个都不……
  ┗ **none of……** 三个以上都不……
  ┏ **both of……** 两个都……
  ┗ **all of……** 三个以上都……
+ **apply oneself to sth.** 努力/致力于做某事（to作介词）
  **= work hard at sth.**
  ✎ 近来我一直在努力地学习英语。
  Recently I have been <u>applying myself</u> assiduously <u>to</u> studying English.
+ **propose** v.(fml.) 打算 to intend to do something
  **propose to do sth.** 打算做某事
  ✎ How do you <u>propose to deal</u> with the situation? 你打算如何处理这种情况？
  **propose doing sth.** 打算做某事
  ✎ How do you <u>propose getting</u> home? 你打算怎么回家？
> 仿写第2段第2句
  连续数年(for years on end)每天早晨锻炼身体需要很强的自制力。
  The self-discipline <u>required to do physical exercises every morning for years on end</u> is considerable.
+ **nevertheless, nonetheless, still, all the same, just the same** 尽管如此，还是……（L2）
  ✎ ‘You certainly did give me a surprise!’ said the vicar. ‘You’ve probably woken up everyone in the village as well. <u>Still,</u> I’m glad the bell is working again.’（L2）
  ✎ ‘<u>Just the same</u>, I’m glad the bell is working again.’（L2课后题-12）
  ✎ The girl is not beautiful. <u>Still/ Nevertheless/ ……</u> , I like her very much. 
+ **creep** v. 蹑手蹑脚地走
  ✎ One bad winter we watched the river <u>creep</u> up the lower meadows.（L56）
+ **about [英]/ around [美]** ad. 各处，到处
  ✎ As there are so many people <u>about</u>, the dogs have to be kept in a special enclosure.（L8）
  辨：
  **round about** ad. 在附近，在周围（L42）
  ✎ <u>Round about</u>, piles of limestone glistened in all the colours of the rainbow.（L42）
+ **twist** v. 转动，扭曲，缠绕
  **twist…… into……** 把……扭曲/缠绕成……
  ✎ We <u>twisted</u> the bed sheets <u>into</u> a rope and escaped by climbing down it. 我们把床单拧成绳子，爬下绳子逃跑了。
+ **frame** n. human or animal body（人或动物的）身体
  ✎ Sobs shook her slender frame. 她抽泣着，苗条的身体都在颤动。
+ ┏ ……, I sat down at the breakfast table <u>in an exhausted condition</u>.（原文）
  ┗ ……, I sat down at the breakfast table <u>exhausted</u>.（原文）
  划线部分既可看作方式状语，又可看作主语补足语。如果看作主语补足语，则可换用形容词表达。
  ✎ Inevitably you arrive at your destination <u>almost exhausted</u>.（L44）
+ It was this that betrayed me.（原文）（this是代词，that是连词）
  **It was…… that ……** 不是……正是……（强调句）
+ **troop** v. 成群结队而行 to walk somewhere together as a group
  ✎ The bell rings and they all <u>troop</u> into school. 铃响了，他们都成群结队地走进学校。
+ **unsettling = disturbing** a. 令人不安的
  **unsettle = disturb** v.
+ **fend <u>sb./sth. 🗘 off</u>** 挡开，躲避开，抵御住
  ✎ He tried to kiss her but she <u>fended</u> him <u>off</u>. 他试图吻她，但她挡开了他。
  ✎ She managed to <u>fend off</u> awkward questions. 她设法避开了令人尴尬的问题。
+ **taunt, jibe/ gibe** 讥笑，嘲弄
  **taunts and jibes** 嘲讽（固定搭配）
  同结构短语：
  **aches and pains** 这疼那疼
  **schemes and intrigues** 阴谋诡计
  **hustle and bustle** 忙忙碌碌
+ **wane** 月亏；减弱（L38）
  **wax and wane** 月圆月亏；兴衰、盛衰
  ✎ Dynasties <u>waxed and waned</u> throughout the history. 在历史上王朝盛衰交替。
  近义替换：
  **ebb (away)** 退潮；减退（**flow** 涨潮）
  **subside** 平息
  ┏ However, my enthusiasm <u>waned</u>.（原文）
  ┗ However, my enthusiasm <u>ebbed (away)/ subsided</u>.（同义替换）
+ **diminish** (fml.) : **reduce, decrease** 减少
+ **gradually, slowly, little by little, bit by bit, by degrees** 逐渐地，慢慢地，一点一点地
+ **<u>fall/ drop</u> to……** 下降到……（L8）
  ✎ The temperature <u>drops to</u> -30° and very few people attempt to cross the Pass.（L8）
  **<u>plunge/ dive</u> to……** 大幅下降，骤降，暴跌
+ **be back to where…… start from** 前功尽弃
  **bring…… back to where…… start from** 使……前功尽弃
  ✎ 一个根本性的错误使我们前功尽弃。
  A fundamental error <u>brought</u> us <u>back to where</u> we <u>had started from</u>.
  **pick up where we left off** 从中断的地方继续（习语）
  ✎ After lunch shall we <u>pick up where we left off</u>? 吃完午饭我们接着干吧？
+ **fresh** a. 精神饱满的（L44）
  ✎ However you decide to spend your time, one thing is certain: you will arrive at your destination <u>fresh</u> and uncrumpled.（L44）
  **keep one’s mind fresh** 使某人精神饱满
  ✎ A cup of coffee will <u>keep your mind fresh</u> in class.
+ **glue** vt. 粘住；n. 胶水
  **be glued to sth.** 全神贯注于某事
  ✎ We <u>were glued to</u> the television watching the election results. 我们全神贯注地盯着电视看选举结果。
> 仿写第2段倒数第6句
  抵制着去睡觉的诱惑，我坐在书房里全神贯注地看《新概念英语》。
  Resisting the temptation to go to bed, I sat in my study with my eyes glued to ‘New Concept English’.

+ **undoing** n. 某人失败的原因
  **be one’s undoing** 是某人失败的原因
  ✎ Slack defense <u>was the team’s undoing</u>. 松懈的防守是球队失败的原因。
  **prove to be one’s undoing** 被证明是某人失败的原因
  ✎ 缺乏经验被证明是他失败的原因。
  Lack of experience <u>proved to be his undoing</u>.
  相关词：
  **downfall**（L36）
  + n1. 垮台
    ✎ Greed led to his <u>downfall</u>. 贪婪导致了他的垮台。
    ✎ A long-lost brother, who was presumed dead, was really alive all the time and wickedly plotting to bring about the hero’s <u>downfall</u>.（L36）
  + n2. 失败，垮台的原因
    **be one’s downfall** 是某人失败/垮台的原因
    ✎ His vanity <u>was his downfall</u>. 他的虚荣心是他垮台的原因。
    **prove be one’s downfall** 被证明是某人失败的原因
    ✎ An addiction to gambling <u>proved to be her downfall</u>. 赌博成瘾被证明是她失败的原因。
+ **<u>doze off/ nod off</u>** 打盹（本不想睡，但仍然犯困）
  **<u>take/ have</u> a nap** 小睡一会，打个盹（主动想睡）
  ✎ I usually <u>take a nap</u> after lunch.
+ **get <u>round/ around</u> to <u>sth./ doing</u>** 有时间做某事（尤其用于否定句）
  ┏ ……, but I just haven’t had time to read it!（原文）
  ┗ ……, but I have never <u>got round/ gotten around to</u> reading it.（同义替换）

---

## **Lesson 51 - Predicting the future**
### **课文原文** [🌏](#第三册目录)
<font color=gray size=4>Predicting the future is notoriously difficult. Who could have imagined, in the mid 1970s, for example, that by the end of the 20th century, computers would be as common in people’s homes as TV sets? In the 1970s, computers were common enough, but only in big business, government departments, and large organizations. These were the so-called mainframe machines. Mainframe computers were very large indeed, often occupying whole air-conditioned rooms, employing full-time technicians and run on specially-written software. Though these large machines still exist, many of their functions have been taken over by small powerful personal computers, commonly known as PCs.

In 1975, a primitive machine called the Altair, was launched in the USA. It can properly be described as the first ‘home computer’ and it pointed the way to the future. This was followed, at the end of the 1970s, by a machine called an Apple. In the early 1980s, the computer giant, IBM produced the world’s first Personal Computer. This ran on an ‘operating system’ called DOS, produced by a then small company named Microsoft. The IBM Personal Computer was widely copied. From those humble beginnings, we have seen the development of the user-friendly home computers and multimedia machines which are in common use today.

Considering how recent these developments are, it is even more remarkable that as long ago as the 1960s, an Englishman, Leon Bagrit, was able to predict some of the uses of computers which we know today. Bagrit dismissed the idea that computers would learn to ‘think’ for themselves and would ‘rule the world’, which people liked to believe in those days. Bagrit foresaw a time when computers would be small enough to hold in the hand, when they would be capable of providing information about traffic jams and suggesting alternative routes, when they would be used in hospitals to help doctors to diagnose illnesses, when they would relieve office workers and accountants of dull, repetitive clerical work. All these computer uses have become commonplace. Of course, Leon Bagrit could not possibly have foreseen the development of the Internet, the worldwide system that enables us to communicate instantly with anyone in any part of the world by using computers linked to telephone networks. Nor could he have foreseen how we could use the Internet to obtain information on every known subject, so we can read it on a screen in our homes and even print it as well if we want to. Computers have become smaller and smaller, more and more powerful and cheaper and cheaper. This is what makes Leon Bagrit’s predictions particularly remarkable. If he, or someone like him, were alive today, he might be able to tell us what to expect in the next fifty years.</font>


### 🌻 **单词讲解**
+ **notoriously** ad. 臭名昭著地，（坏事）众所周知地
  ✎ Predicting the future is <u>notoriously</u> difficult.（本文）
  ✎ The local bus service is <u>notoriously</u> unreliable. 当地的公共汽车服务出了名的不可靠。
  **notorious = infamous** a. 臭名昭著的，（坏事）众所周知的 famous or well-known for something bad
  ✎ a <u>notorious</u> <u>criminal/ area/ bend in the road</u> 一个臭名昭著的罪犯/地区/路口拐弯处
  **be notorious for……** 因……而臭名昭著（作表语）
  ✎ The city <u>is notorious for</u> its bumper-to-bumper traffic. 这座城市因为拥堵的交通而臭名昭著。
  **notoriety** n. 恶名，臭名
  **<u>gain/ achieve</u> notoriety <u>for/ as</u>……** 因/作为……而臭名昭著
  ✎ She <u>achieved notoriety for</u> her affair with the senator. 她因与参议员有染而臭名昭著。
  ✎ He <u>gained a certain notoriety as</u> a gambler. 他作为赌徒而声名狼藉。
  + “著名的”
    **well-known**（偏中性）
    **famous, noted, notable, eminent, celebrated, renowned**（褒义）
  + “不知名的”
    **unknown, little-known, obscure**
+ **technician** n. 技术员，技师
  英文释义：someone whose job is to check equipment or machines and make sure that they are working properly
  ✎ a laboratory <u>technician</u> 实验室技术员
  ✎ a hospital <u>technician</u> 医院技术员
  + 词根 **-ian** = specialist 专家，专业人士
    librar<u>ian</u> 图书管理员
    histor<u>ian</u> 历史学家
    music<u>ian</u> 音乐家
    electric<u>ian</u> 电工
    mathematic<u>ian</u> 数学家
    physic<u>ian</u> 医师；(尤指)内科医生
    pediatric<u>ian</u> 儿科医生
+ **user-friendly** a. 易用的，易理解的，易操作的 easy to use, understand, or operate
  ✎ a <u>user-friendly</u> <u>interface/ printer</u> 易用的界面/打印机（作定语）
  ✎ Computer programs have become more <u>user-friendly</u>. 计算机程序变得更加易用。（作表语）
  **-friendly**
  1. suitable for particular people to use 易用的
    ✎ a **user-friendly** computer program 易用的电脑程序
    ✎ a **family-friendly** restaurant 适合家庭的饭馆
    ✎ a **customer-friendly** shopping mall 顾客友好型购物中心
    ✎ **customer-friendly** banking facilities 客户友好型银行设施
  2. not harmful 无害的
    ✎ **environment-friendly** products 环保产品
    ✎ **ozone-friendly** fridges 对臭氧无害的冰箱
+ **alternative** a. 另外的，其他的，别的（只作定语）
  英文释义：different from something else and able to be used instead of it
  ✎ an <u>alternative</u> <u>plan/ route/ way</u> 备选的/另外的方案/路线/方式
  ✎ <u>alternative</u> approaches to learning 另外的学习的方法
  ✎ Have you any <u>alternative</u> suggestions? 你有别的建议吗？
  **alternative** n. 其他的选择
  **viable alternative** 可行的其他选择
  ✎ Is there a <u>viable alternative to</u> the present system? 除了目前的制度外，有其他的可行的替代方案吗？
  **only alternative** 唯一的其他的选择
  ✎ If payment is not received within five days, legal action will be our <u>only alternative</u>. 如果五天内未收到付款，法律诉讼将是我们唯一的选择。
  **have no alternative but to do sth.** 别无选择只能做某事
  ✎ I <u>had no alternative but to</u> report him to the police. 我别无选择，只能向警方举报他。
  形近词：
  **alternate**
  a1.（常作定语）交替的，轮流的 (of two things) happening or following one after the other
  ✎ <u>alternate</u> blue and red stripes 蓝红相间的条纹
  ✎ <u>alternate</u> triumph and despair 交替的胜利和绝望
  ✎ Private cars are banned from the city on <u>alternate</u> days. 在这个城市里，私家车每隔一天就禁止使用。
  a2. = alternative （只作定语）其他的，另外的，别的
  ✎ We can’t get home tonight, because there are no <u>alternate</u> flights. 我们今晚不能回家，因为没有其它航班。
  ✎ I suggest you have an <u>alternate</u> plan in case you are sick on that day. 我建议你有一个备用计划，以防你那天生病。
+ **relieve** v. 减轻，缓解或解除（痛苦、问题等）
  ✎ Drugs helped to <u>relieve</u> the pain. 药物有助于缓解疼痛。
  ✎ Reading helped to <u>relieve</u> the boredom while he was ill. 他生病时读书有助于缓解无聊。
  ✎ The project is designed to <u>relieve</u> traffic congestion on the main routes into the city. 该项目旨在缓解进入城市的主路的交通拥堵。
  **relieve sb. of sth.** 替某人做某事，使某人免于……
  英文释义：to help sb. by taking sth. heavy or difficult from them
  ✎ Let me <u>relieve</u> you <u>of</u> some of your bags. 让我帮你拿几个包吧。
  ✎ The new secretary will <u>relieve</u> us <u>of</u> some of the paperwork. 新秘书将使我们免于一些文书工作。
  ✎ ……, when they (computers) would <u>relieve</u> office workers and accountants <u>of</u> dull, repetitive clerical work.（本文）
  **relief** n. 宽慰，痛苦的缓解或解脱（L39）
  ✎ find a temporary <u>relief</u> 找到了暂时的解脱
  ✎ permanent <u>relief</u> 永久的解脱
  ✎ to my great <u>relief</u> 使我大为宽心的是
  ✎ give immediate <u>relief</u> from pain 立刻缓解疼痛
  ✎ What a <u>relief</u> it was when the boulders suddenly disappeared, giving way to a stretch of plain where the only obstacles were clumps of bushes.（L39）


### 🕹️ **课文讲解**
+ **众所周知，做某事是非常……**
  ✎ 众所周知，缓解(relieve)人口过剩问题非常困难。
  Relieving the problem of overpopulation is notoriously difficult.
  ✎ 众所周知，改掉(give up)一个根深蒂固的(deep-seated)坏习惯非常困难。
  Giving up a deep-seated bad habit is notoriously difficult.
  ✎ 众所周知，北京的交通拥堵问题非常严重。
  The traffic congestion in Beijing is notoriously serious.
+ **could have done**: 与过去事实相反的虚拟语气（不局限于if从句，可单独使用）
  英文释义：used to say that something was a possibility in the past, but did not actually happen
  ✎ I <u>could have been killed</u>. 我当时可能被杀了。
  ✎ He <u>could have escaped</u>, but he chose to stand and fight. 他本可以逃脱，但他选择挺身战斗/挺身而斗。
+ **mid** 中间的（可单独作形容词，也可构成复合词）
  ✎ from <u>mid</u> July to <u>mid</u> August 从七月中旬到八月中旬
  <u>mid-morning</u> coffee 上午咖啡 （afternoon tea 下午茶：low tea (afternoon tea) 矮桌茶-茶几-下午3点到5点-偏社交；high tea 高桌茶-餐桌-傍晚6点左右-偏果腹）
  ✎ <u>Mid-Autumn</u> Festival 中秋节
  ✎ a young woman in her <u>mid-twenties</u> 一个年轻女子在她二十五六岁左右
  ✎ <u>midsummer, midwinter</u> 仲夏/仲冬
  ✎ on <u>Midsummer</u> Eve 仲夏夜（L56）
  相关表达：
  in the <u>early</u> 1970s 在20世纪70年代早期（上叶）
  in the <u>mid</u> 1970s 在20世纪70年代中期（中叶）
  in the <u>late</u> 1970s 在20世纪70年代晚期（下叶）
> 仿写第2句
  比方说，有谁能在20世纪90年代中期想象到，仅仅十年(a mere decade)之后，手机在中国和手表一样常见？
  Who could have imagined, in the mid 1990s, for example, that after a mere decade, mobile phones would be as common in China as watches?
+ **business**（L7、L14）
  [C] 公司
  ✎ They don’t know how to <u>run</u> **a** <u>business</u>.
  ✎ The company began as **a** small <u>family business</u>.
  ✎ Owners of <u>small business**es**</u> will be hit hardest by these tax changes.
  [U]
  **big business** n.[U] large and powerful companies in general 
  ✎ Does <u>big business</u> have more control over our everyday lives than our elected governments? 是不是大企业对我们的日常生活的控制力超过民选政府呢？
+ **so-called**
  a1. 所谓的（通常被称为的）commonly called
  ✎ They’ve found the flight recorder, the <u>so-called</u> black box. 他们找到了飞行记录仪，即所谓的黑匣子。
  a2. 所谓的（错误地被称为的，名不副实的）incorrectly called
  ✎ His <u>so-called</u> friends betrayed him. 他的那些所谓的朋友背叛了他。
+ mainframe n. 主机，大型机 a large powerful computer that can work very fast and that a lot of people can use at the same time
+ **indeed** ad. 的确，确实
  英文释义：used with ‘very’ and an adjective or adverb to emphasize a statement or description
  ✎ Most of the essays were <u>very good</u> <u>indeed</u>. 大多数文章确实很好。
  ✎ Thank you <u>very much</u> <u>indeed</u>. 非常感谢。
+ **occupy** vt. 占据（时间，空间等）（L44）
+ **air-conditioned** a. 装着空调的
  **air conditioner** n. 空调
+ **run** v. 操作，使机器运转 if you run a machine or engine, you make it operate
  ✎ I often <u>run</u> the washing machine more than once a day. 我经常一天不止一次地使用洗衣机。
+ **take over sth.** 接管……，代替……
  ✎ Military leaders <u>took over</u> the government. 军队领袖接管了政府。
  ✎ Computers can thus be built to <u>take over</u> almost any job where a series of actions are repeated over and over again. 因此，计算机被建造为可以接管几乎任何需要反复执行一系列操作的工作。
+ **be known as……** 被称为……
  ✎ He soon made a name for himself and came to <u>be known</u> to the Italians <u>as</u> Giovanni Acuto.（L14）
  **be commonly known as……** 常被称为……
  ✎ The disease <u>is commonly known as</u> Mad Cow Disease. 这种疾病通常被称为疯牛病。
+ **primitive**
  ① a. 原始的，上古的 of or at an early stage of social development
  ✎ <u>primitive</u> <u>culture/ customs/ tribes</u> 原始的文化/习俗/部落
  ② a. 简单的，简陋的 simple and not modern
  ✎ The local hospital care is <u>primitive</u> and unreliable. 当地医院的照护是简单的，不可依赖的。
+ **launch** v. 推出新产品，新书等（L43、L45）
  英文释义：to make a new product, book etc available for sale for the first time
  ✎ The company hopes to <u>launch</u> the new drug by next October. 该公司希望在明年十月推出这种新药。
  ✎ The new model will <u>be launched</u> in July. 新型号将于7月推出。
  ✎ He is going to <u>launch</u> his latest novel. 他很快就要推出他的最新小说了。
  ✎ Shortly after it <u>was launched</u>, the pie committee went to a local inn to celebrate. 船（尤指新船）下水（L43）

+ **describe…… as……** 把A描述为B（L17） **<span id="⚓describe">（🪐）</span>**
  ✎ He <u>described</u> it <u>as</u> ‘a very agreeable situation located within two small hills in the midst of which flowed a great river.’（L17）
  ✎ The old lady thought he was a fussy creature, but since the porter agreed with him, she rang up her daughter and asked for her help in what she <u>described as</u> a little spot of bother.（L58）
+ **point the way (to……)** v. 指明了（……的）方向
  英文释义：to show how something could change or develop successfully
  ✎ It can properly be described as the first ‘home computer’ and it <u>pointed the way to</u> the future.（本文）
  ✎ Recent medical discoveries are already <u>pointing the way to</u> more efficient vaccines. 最近的医学发现已经指明了更有效的疫苗方向。
+ **giant** n. 特大机构，大公司，巨头 a very large and powerful organization
  ✎ the multinational oil <u>giants</u> 跨国石油巨头
  ✎ Japanese electronics <u>giant</u> Sony 日本电子巨头索尼
+ **DOS** (Disk Operating System) 磁盘操作系统
  英文释义：the basic software in a computer that makes it work and allows you to use a program. It is usually used only in older computers.
+ **copy = imitate** v. 模仿 to behave or do sth. in the same way as sb. else
  ✎ She <u>copies</u> everything her sister does. 她模仿她姐姐所做的一切。
  ✎ Their tactics have <u>been copied</u> by other terrorists. 他们的战术已被其他恐怖分子效仿。
+ **humble**
  a1. 谦虚的
  ✎ He was a genuinely <u>humble</u> man. 他是一个真正谦逊的人。
  a2. 地位卑微的
  ✎ men of <u>humble</u> birth 出身卑微的人
  ✎ a <u>humble</u> occupation 卑微的职业
  a3. 简单的，简陋的 simple and with only basic equipment or features
  ✎ They lived in a <u>humble</u> two-roomed apartment. 他们住在一套简陋的，有两个房间的公寓里。
+ **be in use**: a machine, place etc. that is in use is being used（机器，场所等）在使用，得到使用
  ✎ Electric vehicles built in 1920 were still <u>in use</u> in the 1950s. 1920年制造的电力交通工具在20世纪50年代仍在使用。
  ✎ I’ll be glad to see the building <u>in use</u> again. 我很高兴看到这座建筑再次得到使用。
  ↓ 常加形容词限定
  ✎ From those humble beginnings, we have seen the development of the user-friendly home computers and multimedia machines which are <u>in common use</u> today.（本文）
  ✎ So was born the echo-sounding apparatus, now <u>in general use</u> in ships.（B4L7）
+ **considering** prep.&conj. 考虑到……，鉴于……
  英文释义：in view of (the fact that); taking into consideration
  ✎ <u>Considering</u> the amount she paid, he was dear in more ways than one!（L19-介词）
  ✎ <u>Considering (that)</u> he’s only just started, he knows quite a lot about it. 考虑到他才刚刚开始，他对这件事了解很多了。
+ **as long ago as…… = as early as……** 早在……就……（L14）
  ✎ <u>As long ago as</u> the fourteenth century, an Englishman, Sir John Hawkwood, made the remarkable discovery that people would rather pay large sums of money than have their life work destroyed by gangsters.（L14）
  辨：
  **as long as……**
    1. 长达……（第2个as作介词，后跟名词）
    ✎ It can take <u>as long as</u> <u>eight days</u> to rig up rope ladders and to establish supply bases before a descent can be made into a very deep cave.（L42）
    2. 只要 = **so long as = provided = on condition (that)**（第2个as作连词，后跟从句）
    ✎ Anthropology was by definition impossible, <u>as long as</u> these distinctions between ourselves and the primitive, ourselves and the barbarian, ourselves and the pagan, held sway over people’s minds.（B4L44）
    ✎ ‘<u>So long as</u> there’s something to identify, we will give people their money back,’（L7）
+ **dismiss**
  v1. 解雇，辞退 to remove someone from their job
  ✎ The poor girl <u>was dismissed</u> instantly.（L49）
  v2. 对……不予理会，对……不屑一顾 to refuse to consider sb’s idea, opinion etc, because you think it is not serious, true, or important
  ✎ The government has <u>dismissed</u> criticisms that the country’s health policy is a mess. 政府对该国卫生政策一团糟的批评未予理会。
+ **do sth. for oneself** 亲自……，独立……（L29、L46）
  ✎ The following example of ‘sick humour’ will enable you to judge <u>for yourself</u>.（L29）
  ✎ So great is our passion for doing things <u>for ourselves</u>, that we are becoming increasingly less dependent on specialized labour.（L46）
+ **in those days** 在当年，在当初（L4）
  ✎ <u>In those days</u>, boxers fought with bare fists for prize money.（L21）
  **these days** 当今，现如今
  ✎ <u>These days</u>, people who do manual work often receive far more money than people who work in offices.（L4）
+ **foresee** vt. (foresaw, foreseen) 预见……（L33、L42）
  ✎ The disaster could not have <u>been foreseen</u>. 这场灾难是不可能被预见的。
  ✎ Few analysts <u>foresaw</u> that oil prices would rise so steeply. 很少有分析师预见到油价会急剧上涨。
  ✎ The telephone rings and this marks the prelude to an <u>unforeseen</u> series of catastrophes.（L33）
  **foresight** n. 远见，先见之明
  ✎ Such undertakings require the precise planning and <u>foresight</u> of military operations.（L42）
  **have the foresight to do sth.** 有做某事的远见
  ✎ They <u>had the foresight to</u> invest in new technology. 他们有投资新技术的远见。
  相关词：
  **forethought** n. 远虑，提前的思考
  ✎ With a little <u>forethought</u> many accidents could be avoided. 如果事先稍微多想想，许多事故是可以避免的。
  **forecast** n. 预测，预报
  ✎ weather <u>forecast</u>  天气预报
  **foretell/ predict** v. 预言……
  ✎ Precautions of this sort are necessary, for it is impossible to <u>foretell</u> the exact nature of the difficulties which will confront the pot-holer.（L42）
  ✎ Considering how recent these developments are, it is even more remarkable that as long ago as the 1960s, an Englishman, Leon Bagrit, was able to <u>predict</u> some of the uses of computers which we know today.（本文）
  **foretell** 预兆，预示
  ✎ Timely snow <u>foretells</u> a bumper harvest. 及时的雪预示着大丰收。（瑞雪兆丰年）
  **mark the prelude to sth.** 预示着……，标志着……的序幕/前奏（L33）
  ✎ The telephone rings and this <u>marks the prelude to</u> an unforeseen series of catastrophes.（L33）
+ ┏ **traffic jam<u>s</u>** [pl.]
  ┏ **traffic congestion** [U]
  ┗ 交通堵塞
