+ **diagnose** v. 论断
  ✎ The test is used to <u>diagnose</u> a variety of diseases. 此项测试可用于诊断多种疾病。
  **diagnose sth. as……** 把……诊断为是（某种疾病）
  ✎ The illness <u>was diagnosed as</u> cancer. 此病被诊断为癌症。
  **diagnose sb. <u>as/ with</u>……** 把某人诊断为患有（某种疾病）
  ✎ She <u>was diagnosed as/ with</u> having diabetes. 她被诊断为患有糖尿病。
+ **relieve sb. of sth.** 替某人做某事，使某人免于……
  英文释义：to help sb. by taking sth. heavy or difficult from them
  ✎ Let me <u>relieve</u> you <u>of</u> some of your bags. 让我帮你拿几个包吧。
  ✎ The new secretary will <u>relieve</u> us <u>of</u> some of the paperwork. 新秘书将使我们免于一些文书工作。
+ **repetitive** a. 重复性的（贬义） done many times in the same way, and boring
  ✎ <u>repetitive</u> <u>work/ tasks/ jobs</u> 重复性的工作/任务/职位
  **repetition** n. 重复
  **repeat** v. 重复
+ **clerk**
  n1. 文书；办事员；事务员 person employed in an office, a shop, etc to keep records, accounts, etc.
  n2.(AmE) 店员，售货员 assistant in a shop
  **clerical** a. 文书或办事员的 of, for or made by a clerk or clerks
  ✎ routine <u>clerical</u> work 例行的文书工作
  ✎ administrative and <u>clerical</u> staff 管理人员和办事人员
+ **commonplace** a.(fml.) 寻常的，司空见惯的，不足为奇的
  英文释义：happening or existing in many places, and therefore not special or unusual
  ✎ Car thefts are <u>commonplace</u> in this part of town. 汽车盗窃在城里的这一地区司空见惯。
  ✎ Computers are now <u>commonplace</u> in primary classrooms. 计算机现在在小学教室里很常见。
  **become commonplace** 变得司空见惯
  ✎ Foreign vacations have <u>become commonplace</u>. 去国外度假已经变得很平常了。
  **regard sth. as commonplace** 把某事看作是不足为奇的
  ✎ Such actions <u>were regarded as commonplace</u> during the war. 这种行为在战争期间被认为是司空见惯的。
+ **<u>can’t/ couldn’t</u> possibly……** （强调）不能或不可能……
  英文释义：used to emphasize that you cannot do sth., or that sth. cannot or could not happen or be done
  ✎ I <u>can’t possibly</u> allow you to go home in this weather. 这种天气我不可能让你回家。
  ✎ She <u>couldn’t possibly</u> have heard what was said. 她不可能听说过刚才说的话。
+ **possibly 经常与can/ could连用以表示“尽全力”的意思，**
  **后跟动词时，结构为：<u>can/ could</u> possibly + 动词；**
  **后省略动词时，结构为：possibly <u>can/ could</u>。**（复制自L39）
  ✎ No matter what the conditions were, he believed that a car should <u>be driven</u> as fast as it <u>**could possibly** go</u>.（L39-前后动词不一样，无法省略）
  ✎ She’s <u>done</u> everything she <u>**could possibly** think of</u> to help. 她为了帮忙，已经做了一切她能想到的事情。
  ✎ We shall be <u>contributing</u> as much as we <u>**possibly can**</u> to the campaign. 我们应该尽我们所能为这场运动做出贡献。（省略了动词contribute）
  ✎ Doctors <u>did</u> everything they <u>possibly could</u> to save his life. 医生们为挽救他的生命，竭尽了全力。（省略了动词do）
+ **instant communication** 即时交流沟通
  **IM (instant messaging)** 即时通讯 a type of service available on the Internet that allows you to quickly exchange written messages with people that you know
+ 否定词nor位于句首，引起部分倒装（复习）
  ✎ <u>Nor</u> <u>is</u> the city without its moments of beauty.（L41）
+ **so**
  ① 以便于（有情态动词）-目的状语从句
  ② 所以（无情态动词）- 结果状语从句
+ **越来越……**
  + 比较级 + er；最高级 + est ⇨ 两个比较级连用
    ✎ small<u>er</u> and small<u>er</u>
    ✎ cheap<u>er</u> and cheap<u>er</u>
  + 比较级 + more；最高级 + most ⇨ <u>more and more/ increasingly/ ever more</u> + 原形
    ┏ <u>more and more</u> powerful
    ┗ <u>increasingly</u> powerful
    ┗ <u>ever more</u> powerful

#### 👾 **“疑问词 + to do” 可以视为名词性从句的缩略形式（L38）**
1. 相当于宾语从句
  ↓ They will hardly know <u>which facts to select from……</u>（L38）
  ↳ They will hardly know <u>which facts they should select from……</u>
  ↓ ……, he might be able to tell us <u>what to expect in the next 50 years</u>.（本文）
  ↳ ……, he might be able to tell us <u>what we should expect in the next 50 years</u>.
2. 相当于主语从句
  ↓ <u>Who to turn to</u> is what she wants to know. 她想知道该向谁求助。
  ↳ <u>Who she should turn to</u> is what she wants to know.
3. 相当于表语从句
  ↓ The problem she faces is <u>which way to take</u>. 她面临的问题是该走哪条路。
  ↳ The problem she faces is <u>which way she should take</u>.
4. 相当于同位语从句
  ↓ The problem <u>which course to take</u> worried Lucy for hours. 选哪门课的问题让露西忧虑了好几个小时。
  ↳ The problem <u>which course she should take</u> worried Lucy for hours.

---

## **Lesson 52 - Mud is mud**
### **课文原文** [🌏](#第三册目录)
<font color=gray size=4>My cousin, Harry, keeps a large curiously-shaped bottle on permanent display in his study. Despite the fact that the bottle is tinted a delicate shade of green, an observant visitor would soon notice that it is filled with what looks like a thick, greyish substance. If you were to ask Harry what was in the bottle, he would tell you that it contained perfumed mud. If you expressed doubt or surprise, he would immediately invite you to smell it and then to rub some into your skin. This brief experiment would dispel any further doubts you might have. The bottle really does contain perfumed mud. How Harry came into the possession of this outlandish stuff makes an interesting story which he is fond of relating. Furthermore, the acquisition of this bottle cured him of a bad habit he had been developing for years.

Harry used to consider it a great joke to go into expensive cosmetic shops and make outrageous requests for goods that do not exist. He would invent fanciful names on the spot. On entering a shop, he would ask for a new perfume called ‘Scented Shadow’ or for ‘insoluble bath cubes’. If a shop assistant told him she had not heard of it, he would pretend to be considerably put out. He loved to be told that one of his imaginary products was temporarily out of stock and he would faithfully promise to call again at some future date, but of course he never did. How Harry managed to keep a straight face during these performances is quite beyond me.

Harry does not need to be prompted to explain how he bought his precious bottle of mud. One day, he went to an exclusive shop in London and asked for ‘Myrolite’. The shop assistant looked puzzled and Harry repeated the word, slowly stressing each syllable. When the woman shook her head in bewilderment, Harry went on to explain that ‘myrolite’ was a hard, amber-like substance which could be used to remove freckles. This explanation evidently conveyed something to the woman who searched shelf after shelf. She produced all sorts of weird concoctions, but none of them met with Harry’s requirements. When Harry put on his act of being mildly annoyed, the assistant promised to order some for him. Intoxicated by his success, Harry then asked for perfumed mud. He expected the assistant to look at him in blank astonishment. However, it was his turn to be surprised, for the woman’s eyes immediately lit up and she fetched several bottles which she placed on the counter for Harry to inspect. For once, Harry had to admit defeat. He picked up what seemed to be the smallest bottle and discreetly asked the price. He was glad to get away with a mere twenty pounds and he beat a hasty retreat, clutching the precious bottle under his arm. From then on, Harry decided that this little game he had invented might prove to be expensive. The curious bottle, which now adorns the bookcase in his study, was his first and last purchase of rare cosmetics.</font>


### 🌻 **单词讲解**
+ **tint** v. 染色，微染
  英文释义：to slightly change the colour of something
  ✎ She’s had her eyelashes <u>tinted</u>. 她染了眼睫毛。
  ✎ Despite the fact that the bottle <u>is tinted</u> a delicate shade of green, ……（本文）
  **dye** v. 染色，浸染 colour sth.,esp by dipping in a liquid（L16）
  ✎ <u>dye</u> one’s hair 染发
  ✎ <u>dye</u> a white dress blue 把一件白色的裙子染成蓝色
  ✎ Its wool, which had <u>been dyed</u> black, had been washed clean by the rain!（L16）
  **stain** v. 染色，渍染，着色 colour (wood, fabric, etc) with a substance that penetrates the material
  ✎ He <u>stained</u> the wood dark brown. 他把木头染成了深棕色。
  ✎ We’ve decided to <u>stain</u> the shelves blue. 我们决定把架子染成蓝色。
  **colour** v. 着色 put colour on (sth.), e.g. by painting, dyeing or staining
  ✎ <u>colour</u> a picture 给图画上色
  ✎ <u>colour</u> a wall green 把墙涂成绿色
+ **dispel** v. 驱散，打消（尤指某人的情绪）
  英文释义：to make sth. go away, esp. a belief, idea, or feeling
  字根 **pel**：push
  ✎ <u>dispel</u> <u>doubts/ fears/ worries/ rumors/ hesitations/ prejudice/ ……</u>
  打消疑虑/恐惧/忧虑/谣言/犹豫/偏见/……
  ✎ This brief experiment would <u>dispel</u> <u>any further doubts</u> you might have.（本文）
  ✎ Reading about them increases our understanding without <u>dispelling</u> <u>our fears</u>.（L54）
  + 词根 **pel** = push
    **pro<u>pel</u>** 推进，驱动
    **re<u>pel</u>** 排斥，使厌恶
    **ex<u>pel</u>** 驱逐，开除
    **com<u>pel</u>** 强迫，迫使
    **im<u>pel</u>** 促使，迫使
    **<u>be/ feel</u> compelled to do** 觉得必须做某事（迫于外力）
    **<u>be/ feel</u> impelled to do** 觉得必须做某事（发自内心）
+ **outlandish = bizarre** a. 稀奇古怪的，非常怪异的 extremely strange and unusual
  ✎ an <u>outlandish</u> hairstyle 怪异的发型
  ✎ dancers in rather <u>bizarre</u> costumes 穿着相当怪异服装的舞者
  近义词：
  **strange, unusual, odd, peculiar** 奇怪的，怪异的（语气没有以上两个重）
  ✎ At the time, this did not strike me as <u>odd</u>.（L37）
  ✎ These <u>peculiar</u> forms not only seemed designed to shock people emotionally, but to give them electric shocks as well!（L18）
  **weird** 奇怪的，古怪的
  ✎ A really <u>weird</u> thing happened last night. 昨晚发生了一件非常奇怪的事情。
  **eccentric** n. 古怪的人；a. 异常的，古怪的（仅指人-无贬义）（L31）
  ✎ True <u>eccentrics</u> never deliberately set out to draw attention to themselves.（L31）
  ✎ His <u>eccentric</u> behaviour lost him his job. 他古怪的行为让他丢了工作。
+ **outrageous** a. 令人震惊的，极其不合理的；非常奇怪的
  + a1. very shocking or unreasonable 令人震惊的，极其不合理的
    ✎ His treatment of his wife is <u>outrageous</u>. 他对待妻子的方式令人震惊。
    ✎ She blames me for causing her father’s death. But that’s <u>outrageous</u>! 她指责我导致了她父亲的死亡。但这太离谱了！
    ✎ Gesticulating wildly, the man acted as if he found my offer <u>outrageous</u>, but he eventually reduced the price to £10.（L28）
  + a2. extremely unusual and slightly amusing or shocking 非常奇怪的
    ✎ <u>outrageous</u> <u>clothes/ behaviour</u> 奇怪的衣服/行为
    ✎ She says the most <u>outrageous</u> things sometimes. 她有时会说出最离谱的话。
    ✎ Harry used to consider it a great joke to go into expensive cosmetic shops and make <u>outrageous</u> requests for goods that do not exist.（本文）
+ **freckle** n.[C] 雀斑 one of the small light-brown spots on the human skin
  ✎ Ann’s face and back are covered with <u>freckles</u>. 安的脸和背上布满了雀斑。
  相关词：
  **mole** n.[C] 痣；鼹鼠 small permanent dark spot on the human skin
  **<u>beauty spot/ beauty mark</u>** n.[C] 美人痣 a small dark mark on a woman’s face -used when you think it is attractive
  **acne** n.[U] 座疮，粉刺
  ✎ Many adolescents suffer from <u>acne</u>. 许多青少年都患有痤疮。
  **dimple** n.[C] 酒窝
  **chin dimple** n.[C] 下巴窝
+ **intoxicate** v. 使醉酒；使陶醉
  **intoxicated**
  a1.(fml.) 醉酒的 drunk
  ✎ The driver was clearly <u>intoxicated</u>. 司机显然喝醉了。
  a2. 陶醉的 feeling so excited or happy about something that you cannot think clearly
  **be intoxicated <u>by/ with</u>……** 对……陶醉
  ✎ He <u>was intoxicated by/ with</u> success. 他陶醉在成功之中。
  ✎ <u>Intoxicated by</u> his success, Harry then asked for perfumed mud.（本文-省略be动词，作非谓语动词）
  有毒的：
  **toxic** n. 毒物；a. 有毒的
  **noxious** a. 有毒的
  **poisonous** a. 有毒的
  ✎ <u>toxic</u> <u>chemicals/ substances/ gases</u> 有毒的化学品/物质/气体
  ✎ Carbon monoxide is a colourless, odourless and <u>noxious</u> gas. 一氧化碳是一种无色、无味、有毒的气体。


### 🕹️ **课文讲解**
+ **mud is mud** 实话实说，坦白地说（习语）
  近义习语：
  **call a spade a spade** 实话实说，坦率地说（spade 铲；(纸牌中的)黑桃）
  **tell it like it is** 实话实说
  **tell somebody straight** 实话实说
  ✎ I <u>told her straight</u> that she was wrong. 我坦白地告诉她，她错了。
  **to be <u>honest/ frank</u>**
  **frankly**
  ✎ <u>To be honest/ frank,/ Frankly,</u> George isn’t very good at the job. 坦率地说，乔治不太擅长这份工作。
+ **keep** v. 在某处存放或放置某物 have sth. in a particular place
  ✎ Where do you <u>keep</u> the cutlery? 你把刀叉放在哪了？
  ✎ Always <u>keep</u> your driving licence in a safe place. 要始终将驾照放在安全的地方。
  ✎ George <u>kept</u> a bottle of whiskey under his bed. 乔治在床下放了一瓶威士忌。
+ **curiously-shaped** 奇形怪状的（连字符可有可无）（L18）
  **shaped** 表示某种形状的
  ✎ <u>oddly shaped</u> forms（L18）
  ✎ <u>curiously shaped</u> bits of metal（L46）
  ✎ She has a <u>perfectly shaped</u> figure. 她有着完美的体型。
  ✎ <u>heart-shaped</u> 心形的 ✎ <u>pear-shaped</u> 梨形的 ✎ <u>V-shaped</u> “V”字型的
+ **on display = on show** 展示，陈列（L18）
  ✎ A collection of photographs was <u>on display</u> in the hall. 大厅里展出了一组收藏照片。
  ✎ Even people who take no interest in art cannot have failed to notice examples of modern sculpture <u>on display</u> in public places.（L18）
  ↓ 加修饰
  ✎ …… a large curiously-shaped bottle <u>on permanent display</u> in his study.（本文）
  ✎ Her work is <u>on temporary display</u> at the gallery. 她的作品在美术馆临时展出。
  ✎ The locomotive is kept <u>on static display</u> in the National Railway Museum. 这台火车头在国家铁路博物馆静置展出。
> 仿写第1句
  乔治在书房里一直陈列着一枚金牌。
  George keeps a gold medal on permanent display in his study.

+ **despite the fact that……** (fml.) 尽管……
  **= in spite of the fact that……** (fml.)
  **= <u>tough/ although/ even though/ while/ ……</u>**
  **介词+名词+同位语从句 = 普通从属连词**（L4）
  ✎ 
  for the reason that…… (fml.) 因为……（L4）
  = because of the fact that…… (fml.)
  = due to the fact that…… (fml.)
  = on account of the fact that…… (fml.)
  = because……
+ ┏ **delicate/ light** a. 颜色淡的，浅色的
  ┗ **dark/ deep** a. 颜色浓的，深色的
  **bright** a. 颜色亮的，鲜艳的
+ **shade** n. a particular type of red, green, blue etc. 色度
  **shade of……**
  ✎ <u>a delicate shade of</u> green 淡绿色
  ✎ <u>a bright shade of</u> pink 亮粉红色
  ✎ <u>a deep shade of</u> blue 深蓝色
+ **observant** a. 善于观察的，敏锐的 **= perceptive, eagle-eyed**
  **observation** n. 观察
  ✎ powers of <u>observation</u> 观察力
+ **greyish**(BrE)/ **grayish**(AmE) a. 浅灰色的，灰了吧唧的 slightly grey
✎ yellowish, reddish, bluish, greenish, blackish, whitish ……

+ “if”型的虚拟语气复习（L17、L42）
  **与未来趋势相反：**
   **If + S. + should do, S. + <u>would/ should/ could/ might</u> + do**
   **If + S. + <u>did/ were to do</u>, S. + <u>would/ should/ could/ might</u> + do**（表示极其、甚至完全不可能发生）
+ “if”型的虚拟语气 + 倒装（复制自L42）
  条件：
  **① 是“if”型的虚拟语气；**
  **② if从句中出现以下词汇：were，had(助动词)，should；**
  **③ 通常仅用于书面语。**
  形式：
  **把were，had(助动词)，should放到句首，把连词if去掉，其它词排好队即可。**
  ┏ If you <u>**were** to ask</u> Harry what was in the bottle, he would tell you that it contained perfumed mud.（原文）
  ┗ <u>**Were**</u> you <u>to ask</u> Harry what was in the bottle, he <u>would</u> tell you that it contained perfumed mud.（倒装）
+ **perfumed** a. 加香水的，有香味的 pleasant to smell because perfume has been added or used
  ✎ <u>perfumed</u> <u>soap/ candles</u> 有香味的肥皂/蜡烛
+ **rub** 擦，涂抹
  **rub sth. with sth.** 用……来摩擦/涂抹
  ✎ She began <u>rubbing</u> her hair <u>with</u> a towel. 她开始用毛巾擦头发。
  ✎ A crowd of people gathered round him and a lady <u>rubbed</u> his arm <u>with</u> soap and butter, but George was firmly stuck.（L15）
  **rub sth. into sth.**
  **rub salt into the wound** 往伤口上撒盐
  ✎ <u>Rub</u> the cream well <u>into</u> your skin. 把乳霜擦到皮肤上。
+ **came into (the) possession of sth. (fml.) = get sth.**
  ✎ On her father’s death, she <u>came into possession of</u> a vast fortune. 她父亲去世后，她继承了一大笔财产。
  ┏ How did the painting <u>come into your possession</u>?
  ┗ How did you <u>get</u> the painting? 这幅画是怎么落到你手里的?/ 你是怎么得到这幅画的？
+ **stuff** n.[U] (infml.) things 东西，玩意儿
  ✎ I’ve got some sticky <u>stuff</u> on my shoe. 我的鞋上沾了些黏糊糊的东西。
  ✎ Do you call this <u>stuff</u> beer? 你管这玩意儿叫啤酒？
+ **be fond of……** 非常喜欢……（跟人跟事物都可） having a great liking for……
  ✎ I’ve always <u>been</u> very <u>fond of</u> you. 我一直非常喜欢你。（跟人）
  ✎ John<u>’s</u> extremely <u>fond of</u> pointing out other people’s mistakes. 约翰非常喜欢指出别人的错误。（跟事）
+ **relate** 讲述
  **relate sth. (to sb.)**（向某人）讲述某事
  ✎ We know instinctively, just as beekeepers with their bees, that misfortune might overtake us if the important events of our lives <u>were not related to</u> it.（L56）
  ✎ History does not <u>relate</u> whether his friend accepted his medical help, but in all probability he did.（B4L28）
+ 此外，而且，还（L15）
  **furthermore, further**
  **<u>what is more/ what’s more</u>**
  **moreover, besides**
  **in addition, additionally**
+ **acquisition** [U] 获得；[C] 获得的东西
  ✎ the <u>acquisition</u> of language 语言的习得
  ✎ The money will be spent on <u>acquisitions</u> for the university library. 这笔钱将用于大学图书馆的采购。
+ **cure** v. 治愈
  **cure sb.**
  【✔】**cure a disease**
  **cure sb. of a disease**
  辨：
  **heal** 治愈
  **heal sb.**
  **heal sb. of a disease**
  【✘】heal a disease
  **there is no cure for sth.** 某事物没有药物可以治（**cure** n. 药物；疗法）
  ✎ <u>There is no cure for</u> AIDS.
+ **habit** 与动词的搭配
  ◇ <u>develop/ catch/ acquire/ form/ cultivate/ foster</u> a habit 养成一个习惯
  ◇ <u>change/ alter</u> a habit 改变一个习惯
  ◇ <u>correct</u> a habit 纠正一个习惯
  ◇ <u>abandon/ give up/ drop/ discard/ kick</u> a habit 改掉/戒掉一个习惯
+ **expensive** a. 高档的，豪华的（L6）
  ✎ The <u>expensive</u> shops in a famous arcade near Piccadilly were just opening.（L）
+ **cosmetics** n.[pl.] 化妆品（瓶瓶罐罐里的）
  ✎ Lipstick and hair conditioner are <u>cosmetics</u>. 口红和护发素都是化妆品。
  **<u>make-up/ makeup</u>** n.[U] 化妆品（擦在脸上的）
  ✎ girls in <u>heavy make-up</u> 浓妆艳抹的女孩子们
  ✎ She doesn’t <u>wear makeup</u>. 这个女孩素面朝天。
  形近词、易混词：
  **cosmic** 宇宙的；**cosmos** 宇宙
  **comic** 喜剧的；可笑的；滑稽的
  **comet** 彗星
+ **make a…… request for……** 要求想得到某个东西
  ✎ <u>make</u> repeated <u>requests for</u> help 反复地请求得到帮助
  ✎ They have <u>made an</u> urgent <u>request for</u> international aid. 他们已紧急请求国际援助。
  **<u>issue/ make</u> a…… appeal for……** 诚挚地恳求/呼吁……
  ✎ The police have <u>issued a</u> new <u>appeal for</u> information. 警方已发出新的提供信息的呼吁。
  ✎ The girl’s family have <u>made a</u> public <u>appeal for</u> help to try and catch her killer. 女孩的家人公开呼吁得到帮助，试图抓住凶手。
+ **would 和 used to do 类似，都可以表示过去习惯性的动作，**
  如：One day in a week he <u>would</u> spend a whole day in silence.
  **但注意：would 不能用在故事开头，往往在故事开头用 used to do，而后面换为would do,**
  如：We <u>used to</u> work in the same office and we <u>would</u> often have coffee together.（复制自L36）
  ✎ Harry <u>used to</u> consider it a great joke to go into expensive cosmetic shops and make outrageous requests for goods that do not exist. He <u>would</u> invent fanciful names on the spot. On entering a shop, he <u>would</u> ask for a new perfume called ‘Scented Shadow’ or for ‘insoluble bath cubes’. If a shop assistant told him she had not heard of it, he <u>would</u> pretend to be considerably put out. He loved to be told that one of his imaginary products was temporarily out of stock and he <u>would</u> faithfully promise to call again at some future date, but of course he never did.（本文）
  ✎ We are less credulous than we <u>used to</u> be. In the nineteenth century, a novelist <u>would</u> bring his story to a conclusion by presenting his readers with a series of coincidences — most of them wildly improbable.（L36）
+ **on the spot** 在现场，到现场；立刻，马上
  **do sth. on the spot = do sth. immediately** 立刻/马上做某事
  ✎ He had to make a decision <u>on the spot</u>. 他必须马上做决定。/ 他不得不当场做出决定。
+ **on** prep. 刚一 as soon as（作时间状语）
  ✎ What was your reaction <u>on</u> seeing him? 刚一见到他的时候，你是什么反应？
  ✎ The curtain went up <u>on</u> the final act of the play and revealed the aristocrat sitting alone behind bars in his dark cell.（L22）
  **in** prep. 在……过程中 during the act or process of（作时间状语）
  ✎ He tripped <u>in</u> racing for the bus. 他在追公共汽车的过程中绊倒了。
  ✎ <u>In</u> the last act, a gaoler would always come on to the stage with a letter which he would hand to the prisoner.（L22）
  ✎ <u>In</u> seeking independence, they do not sacrifice their human dignity.（L27）
+ **insoluble** a. 不能溶解的 cannot be dissolved; not soluble
  **soluble** a. 能溶解的
  **dissolve** v. 溶解
+ **put out** a. [BrE.] [never before noun] 气愤的，不悦的 annoyed
  ✎ He seemed a bit <u>put out</u> at not having been invited. 他似乎对没有被邀请感到有点生气。
+ ┏ **imaginary** a. 虚构的；想象中的（L46）
  ┗ **imaginative** a. 富于想象力的
  ✎ She is a very <u>imaginative</u> student. She’s always talking about travelling to outer space.
  (A) imaginary; (B) imaginative; (C) imaginable; (D) imagining
+ ┏ **temporarily** ad. 暂时，临时
  ┗ **permanently** ad. 长期，永久
+ **<u>in/ out of</u> stock** （商店中）有/无现货的
  ✎ Have you any grey pullovers <u>in stock</u>? 你们有灰色套头衫现货吗？
  ✎ I’m sorry, that swimsuit is temporarily <u>out of stock</u> in your size. 对不起，你的尺寸的泳衣暂时缺货。
+ **faithfully** ad. 忠诚地，诚恳地
  ✎ He had served the family <u>faithfully</u> for 40 years. 他忠诚地为这个家庭服务了40年。
  ✎ Ann <u>faithfully</u> promised never to tell my secret. 安诚恳地承诺永远不会泄露我的秘密。
+ **call** v. [Br.E.] 在某处短暂停留以拜访某人或做某事 to stop at a house or other place for a short time to see sb. or do sth.
  ✎ She <u>called</u> for a chat. 她来这聊了会天。
  **call in at sth.** 到某处作短暂停留（L25）
  ✎ Will you <u>call in at</u> the supermarket for some eggs and milk? 你能顺路去超市买些鸡蛋和牛奶吗？
  ✎ After crossing the Equator, the captain <u>called in at</u> a port to have a new rudder fitted, but by now the Thermopylae was over five hundred miles ahead.（L25）
+ **at a…… date** 在过去或未来的某时 a time in the past or future
  ✎ The exact details of the plan will be worked out <u>at a later date</u>. 该计划的确切细节将在未来制定。
  ✎ Johnson had agreed <u>at an earlier date</u> to take on the role of chairman. 约翰逊早些时候答应过担任主席一职。
  ✎ The election is scheduled to take place <u>at an unspecified date</u> in the autumn. 选举定于秋季某个未指明的日期举行。
+ **keep a straight face** 板着脸，忍住不笑 stop oneself from smiling and laughing
  ✎ Brian looked ridiculous in leather trousers, and I was desperately trying to <u>keep a straight face</u>. 布莱恩穿着皮裤看起来很可笑，我拼命地想保持一张严肃的脸。
  **straight-faced** a. 板着脸的
  ✎ We laughed, but Chris was <u>straight-faced</u> and seemed a little offended by the joke. 我们笑了，但克里斯板着脸，似乎有点被这个笑话冒犯到了。
+ **be beyond sb.** 某人无法理解 to be too difficult for someone to understand（L40、L41）
  ✎ Why people are prepared to tolerate a four-hour journey each day for the dubious privilege of living in the country <u>is beyond me</u>.（L41）
  **be <u>quite/ completely</u> beyond sb.** 某人完全无法理解
  ✎ It<u>’s quite beyond me</u> why anyone would want to marry him. 我完全无法理解为什么有人会想嫁给他。
  ✎ The system <u>was</u> complicated and <u>completely beyond the learners</u>. 这个系统很复杂，初学者完全无法理解。
+ **prompt** v. 提问或提示以鼓励某人说 to encourage sb. to speak by asking them questions or suggesting words that they could say
  ✎ ‘And then what happened?’ he <u>prompted</u>. “然后发生了什么？”他问道。
  ✎ The speaker was hesitant and had to <u>be prompted</u> occasionally by the chairman. 演讲者犹豫不决，主席不得不偶尔提示一下。
+ **exclusive**
  a. 高级的，高档的 very expensive, and therefore available only to wealthy people
  ✎ an <u>exclusive</u> <u>store/ restaurant/ neighborhood</u> 高档商店/宾馆/社区
  a. 独家的
  ✎ Newspapers and magazines offered the family huge sums for the <u>exclusive</u> rights to publish stories and photographs.（L45）
+ **stress** v. 重读 to pronounce a word or part of a word so that it sounds louder or more forceful
  ✎ The word ‘machine’ <u>is stressed</u> on the second syllable. “机器”这个词在第二个音节上重音。
+ **in bewilderment = in confusion = in puzzlement = in perplexity** 迷惑不解地
  ✎ She looked at him <u>in bewilderment</u>. 她迷惑不解地看着他。
  ✎ Matt stared at her <u>in confusion</u>. 马特迷惑不解地盯着她。
  ✎ She frowned <u>in puzzlement</u>. 她困惑地皱起眉头。
  ✎ Jane looked about <u>in perplexity</u>. 简困惑地环顾四周。
+ **evidently** ad. 明显地；显然地
  **evident** a. 明显的
  **evidence** n. 证据
+ **convey sth. to sb.** 向某人传达/转达/表达……
  ✎ Please <u>convey</u> my good wishes <u>to</u> your parents. 请代我对你父母表示我的诚挚的祝愿。
  ✎ If you see James, do <u>convey</u> my apologies <u>to</u> him. 如果你见到詹姆斯，请务必转达我的歉意。
  ✎ The poem perfectly <u>conveys to the reader</u> the poet’s feelings. 这首诗完美地向读者传达了诗人的感情。
+ ┏ This explanation evidently conveyed something to <u>the woman **who**</u> searched shelf after shelf.（原文）
  ┗ This explanation evidently conveyed something to <u>the woman **and** she</u> searched shelf after shelf.（换用并列句-啰嗦）
+ **sth. after sth.** 一个又一个地（固定搭配）（复制自L37）
  ✎ But when the train dawdled at <u>station after station</u>, I began to wonder.（L37）
  ✎ day <u>after</u> day 一天又一天地
  ✎ week <u>after</u> week 一周又一周地
  ✎ year <u>after</u> year 一年又一年地
  ✎ time <u>after</u> time 一次又一次地
  ✎ He fired <u>shot after shot</u>. 他开了一枪又一枪。
  ✎ Shelley sent him <u>letter after letter</u> to explain the delay. 雪莉一封又一封地给他写信，解释延误的原因。
  ✎ They sent <u>regiment after regiment</u> to attack us. 他们派了一个又一个团来攻击我们。
  ✎ In <u>factory after factory</u> we were shown machines built by the workers themselves. 在一家又一家工厂里，我们看到了工人自己制造的机器。
+ **produce** v. 出示，拿出 if you produce an object, you bring it out or present it, so that people can see or consider it
  ✎ <u>Produce</u> your ticket! 请出示您的票！
  ✎ They made no effort to hide their amusement whenever I <u>produced</u> a packet of sweets from my pocket.（B2L78）
+ ┏ **all <u>sorts/ kinds/ types</u> of sth.**
  ┏ **sth. of all <u>sorts/ kinds/ types</u>**
  ┗ 各种各样的，各式各样的……
  ✎ <u>all sorts of</u> silly jokes（L40）
  ✎ <u>all sorts of</u> weird concoctions（本文）
  ✎ <u>all sorts of</u> indignities（B4L18）
  ✎ vehicles <u>of all kinds</u>（L47）
+ **concoction** n. 调制品，混合物 sth. that has been made out of several things mixed together
  ✎ a <u>concoction</u> of honey, yogurt, oats, and apples 蜂蜜、酸奶、燕麦和苹果的调制品
+ **<u>comply with/ fulfil [英] fulfill [美]/ meet (with)/ satisfy/ suit</u> one’s requirements** 符合/满足需要
  ✎ The new computer system will <u>meet (with) all our requirements</u>. 新的计算机系统将满足我们所有的需要。
+ **put on an act** 装模作样（固定搭配）
  ✎ He wasn’t really angry; he just <u>put on an act</u>. 他并没有真的生气；他只是装模作样。
  **put on sth.** 假装
  ✎ <u>put on</u> a smile 假装微笑
  ✎ <u>put on</u> airs 假装摆架子
  ✎ <u>put on</u> an injured expression 装出一副受伤的表情
+ **expect sb. to do** 以为某人会做某事（固定搭配）
+ **blank** a. 茫然的 showing no feeling, understanding or interest
  ✎ Steve looked <u>blank</u> and said he had no idea what I was talking about. 史蒂夫看起来一脸茫然，说他不知道我在说什么。
  **blank astonishment**（惊讶得）目瞪口呆（固定搭配）
  ✎ a look of <u>blank astonishment</u> 一副目瞪口呆的表情
+ **it is one’s turn (to do sth.)** 轮到某人做某事
  ✎ <u>It’s your turn</u>. 轮到你了。
  ✎ <u>It’s our turn to</u> drive the kids to school this week. 本周轮到我们开车送孩子们上学了。
+ **light up**（因喜悦、兴奋等，脸上或眼中）露出光彩（L11）
  英文释义：if someone’s face or eyes light up, they show pleasure, excitement etc.
  ✎ His eyes <u>lit up</u> with laughter. 他眼中因为欢笑而露出了光彩。
  ✎ Her face <u>lit up</u> with pleasure. 她高兴得脸上露出了光彩。
  ✎ Suddenly, I saw the Officer’s face <u>light up</u>.（L11）
+ ┏ …… she fetched <u>several bottles</u> **which** she placed on the counter for Harry to inspect.（原文-定语从句）
  ┗ …… she fetched <u>several bottles</u> **and** she placed <u>them</u> on the counter for Harry to inspect.（并列句）
+ **(just) for once** 这一回，这一次 used to say that sth. unusual happens, especially when you wish it would happen more often
  ✎ Be honest <u>for once</u>. 这回诚实点吧。
  ✎ <u>Just for once</u>, let me make my own decision. 就这一次，让我自己做决定吧。
  ✎ <u>For once</u> Colin was speechless. 这一次，科林哑口无言了。
+ **<u>accept/ admit/ concede</u> defeat** 认输
  ✎ She is very determined, and will never <u>admit defeat</u>. 她意志非常坚定，并且决不认输。
  ✎ The prime minister <u>conceded defeat</u> and resigned. 首相承认失败并辞职。
+ **discreet** a. 言行小心谨慎的 careful not to cause embarrassment or attract too much attention, especially by keeping something secret
  ✎ The family made <u>discreet</u> enquiries about his background. 这家人谨慎地询问了他的背景。
  ✎ They are very good assistants, very <u>discreet</u> — they wouldn’t go shouting to the press about anything they discovered while working for you. 他们是非常好的助手，非常谨慎——他们不会在为你工作时向媒体声张任何发现。
+ **a mere……** 仅仅……（L34、L37、L39）
  ① a mere 后跟单数名词时 = **only <u>a/ an</u>**
  ② 在其他情况下 a mere = **only**
+ **beat a (hasty) retreat** 赶紧走了
  英文释义：leave a place quickly in order to avoid an embarrassing or dangerous situation
  ✎ The cat <u>beat a hasty retreat</u> when it saw the dog was coming. 看到狗过来，猫赶紧走了。
  ✎ I saw my aunt coming and <u>beat a hasty retreat</u>. 我看见姑妈来了，便赶紧走了。
+ **clutch** v. 紧紧抓住 to hold something tightly because you do not want to lose it
  ✎ She was <u>clutching</u> a bottle of champagne. 她手里紧紧攥着着一瓶香槟。
+ ┏ **from then on** 从那以后
  ┗ **from now on** 从今往后
+ **decide** 不一定译为“决定”，而常常译为“**（在考虑之后）确定，断定，认为**”，尤其是其后加 that 引导的宾语从句时。（L43）
  ✎ The pie committee <u>decided</u> <u>that the best way to transport the dish would be by canal</u>, so they insured it for the trip.（L43）
  ✎ I <u>decided</u> <u>that I must have taken a wrong turning somewhere</u>.（L57）
  ✎ Her first impulse was to go round all the rooms looking for the thieves, but then she <u>decided</u> <u>that at her age it might be more prudent to have someone with her</u>, so she went to fetch the porter from his basement.（L58）
+ **adorn** v.(fml.) 装饰 to decorate sth.
  **adorn sth. with sth.** 某物装饰某物
  ✎ The walls <u>were adorned with</u> paintings. 墙上装饰了绘画。

---

## **Lesson 53 - In the public interest**
### **课文原文** [🌏](#第三册目录)
<font color=gray size=4>The Scandinavian countries are much admired all over the world for their enlightened social policies. Sweden has evolved an excellent system for protecting the individual citizen from highhanded or incompetent public officers. The system has worked so well, that it has been adopted in other countries too.

The Swedes were the first to recognize that public officials like civil servants, police officers, health inspectors or tax-collectors can make mistakes or act over-zealously in the belief that they are serving the public. As long ago as 1809, the Swedish Parliament introduced a scheme to safeguard the interest of the individual. A parliamentary committee representing all political parties appoints a person who is suitably qualified to investigate private grievances against the State. The official title of the person is ‘Justiteombudsman’, but the Swedes commonly refer to him as the ‘J.O.’ or ‘Ombudsman’. The Ombudsman is not subject to political pressure. He investigates complaints large and small that come to him from all levels of society. As complaints must be made in writing, the Ombudsman receives an average of 1,200 letters a year. He has eight lawyer assistants to help him and he examines every single letter in detail. There is nothing secretive about the Ombudsman’s work, for his correspondence is open to public inspection. If a citizen’s complaint is justified, the Ombudsman will act on his behalf. The action he takes varies according to the nature of the complaint. He may gently reprimand an official or even suggest to parliament that a law be altered. The following case is a typical example of the Ombudsman’s work.

A foreigner living in a Swedish village wrote to the Ombudsman complaining that he had been ill-treated by the police, simply because he was a foreigner. The Ombudsman immediately wrote to the Chief of Police in the district asking him to send a record of the case. There was nothing in the record to show that the foreigner’s complaint was justified and the Chief of Police strongly denied the accusation. It was impossible for the Ombudsman to take action, but when he received a similar complaint from another foreigner in the same village, he immediately sent one of his lawyers to investigate the matter. The lawyer ascertained that a policeman had indeed dealt roughly with foreigners on several occasions. The fact that the policeman was prejudiced against foreigners could not be recorded in the official files. It was only possible for the Ombudsman to find this out by sending one of his representatives to check the facts. The policeman in question was severely reprimanded and was informed that if any further complaints were lodged against him, he would be prosecuted. The Ombudsman’s prompt action at once put an end to an unpleasant practice which might have gone unnoticed.</font>


### 🌻 **单词讲解**
+ **evolve** v. 演变，逐渐形成；进化
  + v1. 演变，逐渐形成 to develop and change gradually over a long period of time
    ✎ The school has <u>evolved</u> its own style of teaching. 这所学校已经形成了自己的教学风格。
    ✎ Sweden has <u>evolved</u> an excellent system for protecting the individual citizen from highhanded or incompetent public officers.（本文）
    **evolve from……** 由/从……演变/发展出来
    ✎ Popular music <u>evolved from</u> folk songs. 流行音乐是从民歌演变而来。
    **evolve into……** 演变成/出……
    ✎ The group gradually <u>evolved into</u> a political party. 这个团体逐渐演变成了一个政党。
  + v2. 进化 an animal or plant changes gradually over a long period of time 
    ✎ Animals have <u>evolved</u> camouflage to protect themselves from predators. 动物已经进化出保护色来保护自己免受捕食者的攻击。
    **evolve from……** 由/从……进化
    ✎ Fish <u>evolved from</u> prehistoric sea creatures. 鱼类是由史前海洋生物进化而来的。
    **evolve into……** 进化成/出……
    ✎ Slowly, these tiny organisms <u>evolved into</u> multicelled creatures. 慢慢地，这些微小的生物进化成了多细胞生物。
  + **evolution** n. 进化；演变，逐渐发展
    ✎ Darwin’s theory of <u>evolution</u> 达尔文的进化论
    ✎ the <u>evolution</u> of farming methods 耕作方法的演变
  + 字根“ **volve/ volu** ” = roll 转
    ◇ e<u>volve</u> 演变；进化（e：向外）
    ◇ in<u>volve</u> 涉及，牵涉（in：在里边）
    ◇ re<u>volve</u> 旋转（in：again）
    ✎ The earth <u>revolves</u> around the sun. 地球绕着太阳转。
    ◇ <u>volu</u>me （成套书籍的）卷；数量；音量
    ◇ e<u>volu</u>tion 演变；进化
    ◇ re<u>volu</u>tion 革命
    ✎ an encyclopedia in 20 <u>volumes</u> 一套20卷的百科全书
    ✎ In politics Britain has preferred <u>evolution</u> to <u>revolution</u>. 在政治上，英国更喜欢渐变而非突变。
+ **over-zealously** ad. 过分热情地
  **overzealous** a. 过分热情的 excessively enthusiastic
  ✎ <u>overzealous</u> movie fans 过分热情的影迷
  ✎ an <u>overzealous</u> manager 一个过份热情的经理
  近义词（复制自L46）
  名词搭配 | 译 | 形容词 | 译 
  ---- | ---- | ---- | ---- 
  enthusiasm for…… | 对于……的热情 | enthusiastic | a. 热情的
  zest for…… | ~ | zestful | a. ~
  zeal for…… | ~ | zealous | a. ~
  ardo(u)r for…… | ~ | ardent | a. ~ 
  passion for…… | ~ | passionate | a. ~ 
+ **qualified** a. 有资格的，有资质的
  英文释义：having finished a training course, or having particular skills, etc.
  ✎ Tim is now a <u>qualified</u> architect. 蒂姆现在是一名有资格的建筑师了。
  **be qualified for……** 对……来说是有资格/资质的
  ✎ What makes you think that you <u>are qualified for</u> this job? 是什么让你认为你有资格胜任这份工作？
  **be qualified to do……** 有资格去做某事
  ✎ I<u>’m</u> not <u>qualified to</u> give advice on such matters. 我没有资格就这类事情提供建议。
  ✎ A parliamentary committee representing all political parties appoints a person who <u>is suitably qualified to</u> investigate private grievances against the State.（本文）
  + **qualify** v.（使）有资格或能力（复制自L49）
    **qualify as** 有……的能力
    ✎ He <u>qualified as</u> a doctor last year. 他去年取得了医生资质。
    **qualify sb. to do sth.** 使某人有能力/有资格做某事
    ✎ The test <u>qualifies</u> you <u>to</u> drive heavy vehicles. 这次考试使你有资格驾驶重型车辆。
    **qualify sb. for sth.** 使某人有资格获得某物
    ✎ This training course will <u>qualify</u> you <u>for</u> a better job. 这门培训课程将使你有资格获得更好的工作。
    ✎ Membership <u>qualifies</u> you <u>for</u> a discount on purchases. 会员身份使您有资格享受购物折扣。
  + **qualification** n.（某工作需要的）资格，能力；文凭，资质证书
    ✎ In addition to all her other <u>qualifications</u>, Bessie was an expert cook.（L49）
+ **secretive** a. 爱保密的，守口如瓶的
  英文释义：liking to keep things secret or to hide one’s thoughts, feelings, etc.
  **be secretive about……** 对……不愿多讲/讳莫如深/守口如瓶
  ✎ He’s <u>being</u> very <u>secretive about</u> his new girlfriend. 他对他的新女友非常保密。
  ✎ There is nothing <u>secretive about</u> the Ombudsman’s work, for his correspondence is open to public inspection.（本文）
  **secret** n.[C] 秘密
  **secrecy** n.[U] 保密 keeping secrets, or state of being secret
  **do sth. <u>in secrecy/ in secret/ secretly</u>** 秘密地做某事
  ✎ Many civilians were slaughtered and buried <u>in secrecy/ in secret/ secretly</u>.
  **in the secrecy of one’s heart** 在某人的内心深处
  ✎ The personable young man is Mary’s true love <u>in the secrecy of her heart</u>. 在玛丽内心深处，这位风度翩翩的年轻人是她的真爱。
  **be <u>veiled/ shrouded/ cloaked</u> in secrecy** 处在隐秘之中
  ✎ The president’s exact itinerary <u>was veiled/ shrouded/ cloaked in secrecy</u> for security reasons. 出于安全考虑，总统的确切行程处在机密之中。
+ **ascertain** vt.(fml.) 查明，弄清，确定
  英文释义：discover sth. so that one is certain
  ✎ The police have so far been unable to <u>ascertain</u> the cause of the explosion. 警方目前还无法确定爆炸的原因。
  **ascertain <u>whether/ what/ how/ etc.</u>** 确定/查明是否如何/是什么/怎么回事等（+宾语从句）
  ✎ We need to <u>ascertain whether</u> the project is feasible. 我们需要确定这个项目是否可行。
  **ascertain that……**
  ✎ The police have <u>ascertained that</u> he knew the victim. 警方已经确定他认识受害者。
  ✎ The lawyer <u>ascertained that</u> a policeman had indeed dealt roughly with foreigners on several occasions.（本文）
+ **prejudiced** a. 有偏见的（贬）
  英文释义：showing an unreasonable dislike for sth. or sb.
  ✎ The media has been accused of presenting a <u>prejudiced</u> view of people with disabilities. 媒体被指责对残疾人持有偏见。（作定语）
  **be prejudiced against……** 对……有偏见（作表语）
  ✎ The early Christian church <u>was prejudiced against</u> the Jews. 早期的基督教会对犹太人持有偏见。
  ✎ The fact that the policeman <u>was prejudiced against</u> foreigners could not be recorded in the official files.（本文）
  近义搭配：
  ┏ **be biased <u>against</u>……** 对……有偏见
  ┗ **be biased <u>in favor of/ toward(s)</u>……** 对……偏袒的（towards [英]；toward [美]）
  ┗ **be partial <u>to/ toward(s)</u>……** 对……偏袒的/偏向的
  ✎ He <u>seemed</u> a bit <u>biased against</u> women in my opinion. 在我看来，他似乎对女人有点偏见。
  ✎ The judge <u>is biased in favor of</u> the plaintiff. 法官偏袒原告。
  ✎ The referee <u>was</u> clearly <u>partial to</u> the other side. 裁判显然偏袒对方。
  **prejudice (against……)** 对……的偏见
  **bias (against……)** 对……的偏见
  **bias (<u>in favor of/ toward(s)</u>……)** 对……的偏袒
  **partiality (<u>to/ toward(s)</u>……)** 对……的偏袒


### 🕹️ **课文讲解**
+ **Scandinavian** n.&a. (native) of Scandinavia (i.e. Denmark, Norway, Sweden, Finland, Iceland)
+ **much 常与过去分词构成的形容词连用，表示“广为……”、“广受……”**（L48）
  ✎ The money will buy <u>much needed</u> books for the school. 这笔钱将为学校购买广受需要的书籍。
  ✎ Education is a <u>much discussed</u> government service. 教育是一项备受讨论的政府服务。
  与过去分词共同构成新的形容词：
  **much-used** 受到广泛使用的
  **much-needed** 受到广泛需要的
  **much-travelled** 游历广的（L48）
  **much-loved** 备受喜爱的
  **much-respected** 备受尊敬的
  **much-admired** 备受钦佩的
  **much-discussed** 广为讨论的
  **much-criticized** 备受批评的
  **much-acclaimed** 备受赞誉的
  ✎ In this <u>much-travelled</u> world, there are still thousands of places which are inaccessible to tourists.（L48）
+ **all over the world** 在世界各地（L23）
  **= throughout the world**
  **= <u>round[英]/ around[美]</u> the world**
  **= in various parts of the world**（L23）
  **= the world over**
  ✎ Cooked in wine, snails are a great luxury <u>in various parts of the world</u>.（L23）
+ **enlighten** 开明的
  ✎ Though my aunt pursued what was, in those days, an <u>enlightened policy</u>, in that she never allowed her domestic staff to work more than eight hours a day, she was extremely difficult to please.（L49）
+ **Sweden** n. 瑞典
  **Swede** n. 瑞典人
  **Swedish** a. 瑞典的，瑞典人的，瑞典语的；n. 瑞典语
  ✎ The <u>Swedes</u> were the first to recognize that……（本文）
  ✎ the <u>Swedish</u> Parliament（本文）
  ✎ a <u>Swedish</u> village（本文）
  辨：
  **Switzerland** n. 瑞士（L8）
  **Swiss** n. 瑞士人（单复同型）；a. 瑞士的，瑞士人的，瑞士方言的
+ **protect…… from……** 保护……以防……
  ✎ The cover <u>protects</u> the machine <u>from</u> dust. 这个罩保护机器以防受到灰尘的损害。
+ **high-handed** a. 专横的，顾指气使的 using authority in an unreasonable way, without considering the opinions of other people
  ✎ She resented his <u>high-handed</u> manner. 她讨厌他专横的态度。
+ **work** v. 有某种效果 to have a particular effect or result
  ✎ The strategy seems to be <u>working</u>. 该策略似乎正在发挥作用/是有效的。
  ✎ Criticizing your former employers <u>works against</u> you in the interview. 在面试中批评你的前雇主对你不利。
  ✎ Carlyle was entirely ignorant of what the bottle in his pocket contained, of the nature of the illness from which his friend was suffering, and of what had previously been wrong with his wife, but a medicine that had <u>worked so well</u> in one form of illness would surely be of equal benefit in another, and comforted by the thought of the help he was bringing to his friend, he hastened to Henry Taylor’s house.（B4L28）
+ **public official** n. 公职人员（以官方的身份行事的人）
  **civil servant = public servant** n. 公务员（政府文职人员）
  **health inspector** n. 卫生检查员 someone who works for the government whose job is to visit restaurants and make sure that they are clean and obeying laws about preparing food
+ **in the belief that…… = because sb. believe that……** 因为某人相信……
  ✎ She wrote to him <u>in the belief that</u> he would help her. 她写信给他，因为她相信他会帮助她。
  **“in the + 表示感觉的名词” 在句中多作原因状语**，意为：因为……。较正式。 **<span id="⚓in the + 表示感觉的名词">（🪐）</span>**
  ◇ **in the belief that……** = because sb. believe that……
  ◇ **in the thought that……** = because sb. think that…… 因为某人认为……
  ◇ **in the discovery that……** = because sb. discover that…… 因为某人发现……
  ◇ **in the hope <u>of doing/ that</u>……** = because sb. hope <u>to do/ that</u>…… 因为某人希望……
  ✎ The Swedes were the first to recognize that public officials like civil servants, police officers, health inspectors or tax-collectors can make mistakes or act over-zealously <u>in the belief that (= because they believe that)</u> they are serving the public.（本文）
  ✎ They leave unwanted objects in drawers, cupboards and attics for years, <u>in the belief that (= because they believe that)</u> they may one day need just those very things.（L59）
  ✎ Young men who have reason to fear that they will be killed in battle may justifiably feel bitter <u>in the thought that (= because they think that)</u> they have been cheated of the best things that life has to offer.（B4L11）
  ✎ In the lift her thoughts were on lunch and a good rest; but when she got out at her own floor, both were forgotten <u>in her sudden discovery that (= because she suddenly discovered that)</u> her front door was open.（L58）
  ✎ The men of our family waded down through our flooded meadows with boathooks, <u>in the hope of being (= because they hope to be)</u> able to grapple a corner of the raft and pull it out of the current towards our bank.（L56）
+ **as long ago as…… = as early as……** 早在……就……（L14、L51）
+ **parliament** n. 国会，议会 group of people who are elected to make a country’s laws and discuss important national affairs
  **Parliament** n. 英国国会（包括下议院和上议院） the main law-making institution in the UK, which consists of the <u>House of Commons（下议院）</u> and the <u>House of Lords（上议院）</u>
  **parliamentary** a. 议会的，国会的
  ✎ a <u>parliamentary</u> committee（本文）
  **Congress** n. 美国国会（包括参议院和众议院） the group of people elected to make laws in the US, consisting of the <u>Senate（参议院）</u> and the <u>House of Representatives（众议院）</u>
  **congressional** a. 美国国会的
  ✎ a <u>congressional</u> committee
+ **introduce** v. 开始推行，开始采用（L21）
  ✎ The use of gloves was not <u>introduced</u> until 1860, when the Marquis of Queensberry drew up the first set of rules.（L21）
+ **scheme** n. ① 计划，方案；② 阴谋诡计（L36、L50）
  ✎ Most of us fail in our efforts at self-improvement because our <u>schemes</u> are too ambitious and we never have time to carry them out.（L50）
  **schemes and intrigues** 阴谋诡计
+ **safeguard** v. 保护，保卫 to protect sth. from harm or damage
  ✎ We hope that world leaders can agree on a plan to <u>safeguard</u> the environment. 我们希望世界各国领导人能够就保护环境的计划达成一致。
  **safeguard <u>sb./ sth.</u> against sth.** 保护/保卫某人某物，以对抗……/以免受到……的伤害
  ✎ The company was blamed for failing to <u>safeguard</u> workers <u>against</u> dangerous chemicals. 该公司被指责未能保护工人免受危险化学品的侵害。
  **safeguard** n. 预防措施
  **safeguard against……** 对于……的预防措施
  ✎ Congress established the law as a <u>safeguard against</u> tax evasion. 国会制定这项法律是为了防止偷税漏税。
+ **appoint** v. 任命，委任 to choose someone for a position or a job
  ✎ They have <u>appointed</u> a new manager. 他们任命了一位新经理。
  **appoint sb. to sth.** 将某人委任到某个岗位
  ✎ It made sense to <u>appoint</u> a banker <u>to</u> this job. 指派一位银行家做这份工作是明智之举。
  **appoint sb. to do sth.** 委任某人做某事
  ✎ A lawyer <u>was appointed to</u> represent the child. 一位律师被委任来代表这个孩子。
  **appoint sb. (as) sth.** 委任某人某职务/头衔
  ✎ They <u>appointed</u> him <u>(as)</u> captain of the English team. 他们任命他担任英国队队长。
+ **grievance** n. 委屈，不平，不满，牢骚 **<span id="⚓grievance">（🪐）</span>**
  英文释义：a complaint or a strong feeling that you have been treated unfairly
  ◇ inviting the members to **air** their **grievances** 邀请成员们表达他们的不满
  ◇ Management agreed to **settle** the workers’ **grievances**. 管理层同意解决工人的不满。
  ◇ Bill still <u>**harbour**s/ **nurse**s</u> a **grievance against** his employers for not promoting him. 比尔仍然对雇主不提拔他心怀不满。
+ **refer to A as B** 把A称为B（L4、L49）
  **call A B**
  **address A as B**
  **know A as B**
  **常与副词 commonly, usually, generally, frequently, often 等连用**
  ✎ The official title of the person is ‘Justiteombudsman’, but the Swedes <u>commonly refer to</u> him <u>as</u> the ‘J.O.’ or ‘Ombudsman’.（本文）
  ✎ Though these large machines still exist, many of their functions have been taken over by small powerful personal computers, <u>commonly known as</u> PCs.（L51）
  ✎ People who work in offices <u>are frequently referred to as</u> ‘white-collar workers’ for the simple reason that they usually wear a collar and tie to go to work.（L4）
+ **be subject to sth.** 可能或易于受到……的影响 likely to be affected by sth., especially sth. bad
  ✎ Flights <u>are subject to</u> delay because of the fog. 航班可能因为雾而延误。
  ✎ Smokers <u>are</u> more <u>subject to</u> heart attacks than non-smokers. 吸烟者比非吸烟者更容易患心脏病。
+ **两个含义相反的形容词连用时，常位于被修饰名词之后。**
  ✎ He investigates complaints **large and small**……（原文）
  ✎ A man with a noble heart never bows before <u>difficulties **great or small**</u>. 一个有高尚心灵的人从不会向大大小小的困难屈服。
  ✎ We should be fair to all <u>people, **big and small**, **young and old**</u>. 我们应该公平对待所有人，无论大小，无论老少。
+ **level** n. 级别，阶层 relative position in rank, class or authority
  ✎ These are subjects for discussion at management <u>level</u>. 这些是管理层讨论的话题。
+ **<u>make/ bring/ file/ lodge/ submit</u> a complaint** <u>about sth./ against sb.</u> 投诉某事/某人
  ✎ I’d like to <u>make a complaint about</u> the noise. 我想投诉一下噪音。
  ✎ He <u>brought a complaint against</u> his former manager. 他对他的前任经理提出了投诉。
  ✎ I determined to <u>lodge a complaint</u> as soon as we arrived.（L37）
  ✎ …… if any further <u>complaints were lodged against</u> him, he would be prosecuted.（本文）
+ ┏ **in writing** 以书面形式
  ┗ **in speech** 以口头形式
  ✎ All bookings must be confirmed <u>in writing</u>. 所有的预订必须以书面形式确认。
  ✎ He expressed his opinions both <u>in speech</u> and <u>in writing</u>. 他通过口头和书面形式表达了自己的观点。
  + **in** 以/用某种形式
  ◇ speak **in English** 用英语来说
  ◇ pay **in cash** 用现金支付
  ◇ a short note scribbled **in pencil** 用铅笔潦草写下的简短便条
  ◇ write a message **in code** 用密码写一条消息
  ◇ The title was printed **in capital letters**. 标题用大写字母印刷。
+ **an average of……** 平均……
  ✎ Parents spend <u>an average of</u> ＄220 a year on toys for their children. 父母每年平均花费220美元给孩子买玩具。
  ✎ Prices have risen by <u>an average of</u> 4% over the past year. 在过去的一年里，价格平均上涨了4%。
  **on (an) average** 平均……
  ✎ My income’s rather variable, but I earn ＄100 a day <u>on average</u>. 我的收入变化很大，但我平均每天挣100美元。
  ✎ As a reasonable guess, they might, <u>on an average</u>, be 100 light years away.（B4L43）
+ <u>lawyer</u> assistants
  名词作定语修饰另外一个名词，通常作单数
+ **every single** 每一……（加强 every 的语气）
  ✎ We eat rice <u>every single</u> day! 我们每一天都吃米饭！
  ✎ Don’t write down <u>every single</u> word I say. 不用把我说的每一个字都写下来。
+ **There is nothing secretive about……** ……没有什么可保密的
  ✎ <u>There is nothing secretive about</u> it. 这事没有什么可保密的。
  ✎ <u>There is nothing secretive about</u> Christianity. 基督教没有什么可保密的。
+ **correspondence** n.[U] 来往信件 the letters that someone sends and receives, especially official or business letters
  **letter** n.[C] 信件
  ✎ She has a lot of <u>correspondence</u> to deal with. 她有大批信件需要处理。
  **mail** n.[U] 邮件 the letters and packages that are delivered to you
  ✎ There isn’t much <u>mail</u> today. 今天没多少邮件。
  ✎ He agreed that a train did come into the station at the time on the paper and that it did stop, but only to take on <u>mail</u>, not passengers.（L60）
+ **open** a. 公开的，开放的，没有限制的 public, not limited
  **be open to <u>sb./ sth.</u>** 对……公开/没有限制
  ✎ The competition <u>is open to</u> anyone over the age of sixteen. 比赛对任何16岁以上的人都开放。
  ✎ I’d like to think I <u>am open to</u> any reasonable suggestion. 我愿意接受任何合理的建议。
+ **justified** a. 合理的 having an acceptable explanation or reason
  **<u>be/ feel</u> justified in doing sth.** 做某事是（感觉）合理的
  ✎ She <u>felt</u> fully <u>justified</u> in asking for her money back. 她觉得要回她的钱是完全合理的。
  **justify** v. 表明或证明……是合理的 to show or prove that sb./ sth. is right or reasonable
  ✎ The end <u>justifies</u> the means. 只要目的正确，可以不择手段。（谚语）
  **justification** n.[U&C] 正当的理由 a good and acceptable reason for doing sth.
  **justification for (doing) sth.** 做某事的正当理由
  ✎ There is no <u>justification for</u> holding her in jail. 没有理由把她关进监狱。
  ✎ In the young there is a <u>justification for</u> this feeling.（B4L11）
+ **<u>on behalf of sb./ on sb.’s behalf</u>** [英]
  **<u>in behalf of sb./ in sb.’s behalf</u>** [美]
  ① 代表，代替 representing; instead of
  ✎ Unfortunately, George cannot be with us today so I am pleased to accept this award <u>on his behalf</u>. 不幸的是，乔治今天不能和我们在一起，所以我很高兴代表他接受这个奖项。
  ② 为了某人的利益 in the interest of sb.
  ✎ The legal guardian must act <u>on behalf of the child</u>. 法定监护人必须为了孩子的利益做事。
  ✎ They campaigned <u>on behalf of asylum seekers</u>. 他们为寻求庇护的人奔走。
+ **take action** 采取行动 do sth. in response to what has happened
  ✎ Immediate <u>action</u> must <u>be taken</u> to stop the fire spreading. 必须立即采取行动以阻止火势蔓延。
  ✎ It was impossible for the Ombudsman to <u>take action</u>,……（本文）
+ **vary <u>according to/ depending on</u>……** 根据……而变化
  ✎ Prices <u>vary according to</u> the type of room you require. 价格因您所需的房间类型而异。
  ✎ The leaf’s size <u>varies widely according to</u> the area where it grows. 叶子的尺寸大小根据植物生长的地区会有很大的变化。
  ✎ Costs are likely to <u>vary depending on</u> where you live. 费用可能因您居住的地方而异。
  ✎ Every solid object will reflect a sound, <u>varying according to</u> the size and nature of the object.（B4L7- vary 作非谓语动词）
+ **<u>reprimand/ rebuke</u> sb. for sth.** 因为某事而批评某人（多用于上下级之间） **（L31）<span id="⚓reprimand">（🪐）</span>**
  ✎ I <u>was reprimanded/ rebuked</u> by my manager <u>for</u> being late. 我因迟到而受到了经理的训斥。
  ✎ Recognizing who the customer was, the manager was most apologetic and <u>reprimanded</u> the assistant severely.（L31）
+ **write to sb. = write a letter to sb.** 向某人写信
+ **ill-treat** v. 虐待 to treat sb. in a cruel or unkind way, abuse
  ✎ <u>ill-treat</u> one’s dog 虐待某人的狗（及物动词）
  ✎ They thought Mr. Smith had been <u>ill-treating</u> his wife. 他们认为史密斯先生一直以来都在虐待他的妻子。（及物动词）
  ✎ <u>ill-treated</u> animals 受虐待的动物（过去分词作形容词）
  ┏ **ill** ad. badly
  ◇ <u>ill</u>-bred 没有良好教养的，缺少家教的（**breed** 哺育）
  ◇ <u>ill</u>-advised 不明智的
  ◇ <u>ill</u>-mannered 没礼貌的
  ┗ **well** ad.
  ◇ <u>well</u>-bred 有良好教养的，有家教的
  ◇ <u>well</u>-advised 很明智的
  ◇ <u>well</u>-informed 消息灵通的
  ◇ <u>well</u>-intentioned 动机很好的，目的很好的
+ ┏ **for the simple reason that……** 只不过是因为……（较后者更正式）（L4、L46）
  ┗ **simply because……**
  ✎ People who work in offices are frequently referred to as ‘white-collar workers’ <u>for the simple reason that</u> they usually wear a collar and tie to go to work.（L4）
  ✎ I was not surprised to find that the machine still refused to work after I had reassembled it, <u>for the simple reason that</u> I was left with several curiously shaped bits of metal which did not seem to fit anywhere.（L46）
  加副词修饰：
  **simply because……** 只不过是因为……
  **partly because……** 部分是因为……
  **mainly because……** 主要是因为……
  ✎ Many exam candidates lose marks <u>simply because</u> they do not read the questions properly. 许多考生只不过是因为没有正确阅读问题而失去分数。
  ✎ I decided to go with them, <u>mainly because</u> I had nothing better to do. 我决定和他们一起去，主要是因为我没有更好的事情可做。
  ✎ Hubert never experienced any fear, and this was <u>partly because</u> he was not particularly intelligent. 休伯特从未经历过任何恐惧，部分是因为他不是特别聪明。
+ **Chief of Police** n. 警察局长 the most senior police officer in a city who is in charge of all the police there
+ **deny <u>an accusation/ a charge</u>** 否认一项指责/指控
  ┏ **accuse sb. of (doing) sth.**（L1）
  ┏ **charge sb. with (doing) sth.**
  ┗ 因为（做）某事控告/指责某人
+ **deal** <u>well/ badly/ etc.</u> **<u>by/ with</u> sb.** (fml.) 对某人好、坏等 treat sb. well, badly etc.
  ✎ He has always <u>dealt well by</u> me. 他总是对我很好。
  ✎ You’ve <u>been badly dealt with</u>. 你受到了不好的对待。
  ✎ The police <u>dealt roughly with</u> the rioters. 警察对待暴乱者非常粗鲁。
  ✎ He <u>deals fairly with</u> all people. 他公平地对待所有人。
  ✎ I consider he has <u>been dealt with leniently</u>. 我认为他受到了慈善的对待。
+ **in question** 正在被讨论的，提到的，谈到的 being discussed
  ✎ The woman <u>in question</u> is sitting over there. 我们正在说的那个女人就坐在那边。
  ✎ The job <u>in question</u> is available for three months only. 我们正在说的这份工作只在这三个月之内能够有机会得到。
+ **lodge a complaint** against sb. 投诉某人（详见本文单词讲解）
+ **prosecute** vt. 检举，起诉，对……提起公诉
  ✎ Trespassers will <u>be prosecuted</u>. 侵入者将被起诉。/闲人免进，违者必究。（**trespass** 非法侵入；**trespasser** 非法侵入者）
  ✎ Shoplifters will <u>be prosecuted</u>. 盗窃者将被起诉。
+ **<u>put/ bring</u> an end to sth.** 终止……，废止…… stop sth. from happening any more; abolish sth.
  ✎ The government is determined to <u>put an end to</u> terrorism. 政府决心终止恐怖主义行为。
  ✎ It’s hoped the talks may <u>bring an end to</u> the violence. 人们希望会谈能够终止暴力行为。
+ **<u>go/ pass</u> unnoticed** 不为人知地过去了（固定搭配）（L45）
  ✎ The event <u>went unnoticed</u>. 这件事悄无声息地过去了。
  ✎ Her death <u>passed unnoticed</u>. 她的死没有引起人们的注意。
  ✎ If they had only had one more child, the fact would have <u>passed unnoticed</u>.（L45）
+ ┏ The Ombudsman’s prompt action at once put an end to an unpleasant practice which might have gone unnoticed.（原文）
  ┗ The Ombudsman’s prompt action at once put an end to an unpleasant practice which <u>might have gone</u> unnoticed (if there <u>had not been</u> the Ombudsman’s prompt action).（补全if从句）

---

## **Lesson 54 - Instinct or cleverness?**
### **课文原文** [🌏](#第三册目录)
<font color=gray size=4>We have been brought up to fear insects. We regard them as unnecessary creatures that do more harm than good. We continually wage war on them, for they contaminate our food, carry diseases, or devour our crops. They sting or bite without provocation; they fly uninvited into our rooms on summer nights, or beat against our lighted windows. We live in dread not only of unpleasant insects like spiders or wasps, but of quite harmless ones like moths. Reading about them increases our understanding without dispelling our fears. Knowing that the industrious ant lives in a highly organized society does nothing to prevent us from being filled with revulsion when we find hordes of them crawling over a carefully prepared picnic lunch. No matter how much we like honey, or how much we have read about the uncanny sense of direction which bees possess, we have a horror of being stung. Most of our fears are unreasonable, but they are impossible to erase. At the same time, however, insects are strangely fascinating. We enjoy reading about them, especially when we find that, like the praying mantis, they lead perfectly horrible lives. We enjoy staring at them, entranced as they go about their business, unaware (we hope) of our presence. Who has not stood in awe at the sight of a spider pouncing on a fly, or a column of ants triumphantly bearing home an enormous dead beetle?

Last summer I spent days in the garden watching thousands of ants crawling up the trunk of my prize peach tree. The tree has grown against a warm wall on a sheltered side of the house. I am especially proud of it, not only because it has survived several severe winters, but because it occasionally produces luscious peaches. During the summer, I noticed that the leaves of the tree were beginning to wither. Clusters of tiny insects called aphids were to be found on the underside of the leaves. They were visited by a large colony of ants which obtained a sort of honey from them. I immediately embarked on an experiment which, even though it failed to get rid of the ants, kept me fascinated for twenty-four hours. I bound the base of the tree with sticky tape, making it impossible for the ants to reach the aphids. The tape was so sticky that they did not dare to cross it. For a long time. I watched them scurrying around the base of the tree in bewilderment. I even went out at midnight with a torch and noted with satisfaction (and surprise) that the ants were still swarming around the sticky tape without being able to do anything about it. I got up early next morning hoping to find that the ants had given up in despair. Instead, I saw that they had discovered a new route. They were climbing up the wall of the house and then on to the leaves of the tree. I realized sadly that I had been completely defeated by their ingenuity. The ants had been quick to find an answer to my thoroughly unscientific methods!</font>


### 🌻 **单词讲解**
+ **wage** v. 发动（战争等）
  **wage <u>war/ a campaign/ a struggle/ a battle</u> <u>on /against</u>……**
  向……发动战争/战役/搏斗/战斗
  ✎ The US <u>waged war on</u> Iraq without UN authorization. 美国未经联合国授权对伊拉克发动了战争。
  ✎ The government determined to <u>wage a campaign against</u> official corruption. 政府决定发起一场反对官员腐败的运动。
  **declare war on……** 向某国宣战
  **be at war with……** 与某国在交战
  ✎ Whenever the Italian city-states <u>were at war with</u> each other, Hawkwood used to hire his soldiers to princes who were willing to pay the high price he demanded.（L14）
+ **provocation** n. 激怒，惹怒
  **at the slightest provocation** 稍微一激惹
  ✎ He’d fly into a rage <u>at the slightest provocation</u>. 稍微一激惹，他就会勃然大怒。（**fly into a rage** 勃然大怒；**rage** 暴怒）
  **without provocation** 没有人惹，无缘无故
  ✎ The soldiers fired <u>without provocation</u>. 士兵们无缘无故地开枪了。
  ✎ They sting and bite <u>without provocation</u>.（本文）
  字根 **voc = voke** 喊叫
  ┏ **provoke** v. 激怒，惹怒，挑衅
  ┗ **provocative** a. 挑衅性的
  ┏ **evoke** v. 唤起，激起（情绪）
  ┗ **evocation** n.（情绪的）唤起，激起
  ┏ **revoke** v. 撤销，废止
  ┗ **revocation** n.（某事物的）撤销，废止
  ✎ Her license was <u>revoked</u>. 她的执照被吊销了。
+ **revulsion** n.[U] 厌恶 = disgust
  英文释义：a strong feeling of shock and very strong dislike
  **do sth. with revulsion** 厌恶地做某事
  ✎ She looked at him <u>with revulsion</u>. 她厌恶地看着他。
  **revulsion <u>at/ against/ towards</u>** 对……的厌恶
  ✎ He expressed his <u>revulsion at/ against/ towards</u> the whale hunting. 他表达了自己对捕鲸的厌恶。
  **revolt** v. 令人厌恶 to make someone feel unpleasantly shocked or disgusted
  **be revolted by……**（被动）
  ✎ We <u>were revolted by</u> the dirt and mess in her house. 我们对她房子里的脏乱非常厌恶。
  **revolting** a. 令人厌恶的 extremely unpleasant
  ✎ Picking your nose is a <u>revolting</u> habit. 挖鼻孔是一种令人厌恶的习惯。
  近义词：（L18、L23）
  v. | a. 
  ---- | ---- 
  repel | repellent 
  repulse | repulsive 
  revolt | revolting 
  disgust | disgusting 
  
  ✎ I <u>was repelled by</u> the smell. 我非常厌恶这股味道。
  ✎ The tourists <u>were repulsed by</u> the filthy conditions. 游客们厌恶这里肮脏的环境。
  ✎ He claimed to <u>be disgusted by</u> the amount of violence in the film. 他声称对电影中的暴力场面感到厌恶。
+ **luscious** a. 美味的，甘美多汁的 having a pleasant sweet taste or containing a lot of juice
  ✎ the <u>luscious</u> taste of ripe peaches 成熟桃子的甘甜味道
  ✎ a <u>luscious</u> and fragrant dessert wine 一种甘甜芳香的甜酒
  近义词：
  **delicious** a. 美味的
  **appetizing** a. 引起食欲的
  **heavenly** a. 美好的；很愉快的
  **tasteful** a. 美味的；雅致的
  **tasty** a. 美味的
  ┏ **yummy**（口）好吃的
  ┗ **yucky**（口）难吃的
  **delicacy** n. 美味，佳肴，好吃的东西（L23）
  ✎ If you lived in the Mediterranean, for instance, you would consider octopus a great <u>delicacy</u>.（L23）
+ **ingenuity** n.[U] 机灵，心灵手巧，善于发明创造
  英文释义：the ability to invent things or solve problems in clever new ways
  **ingenious** a. 机灵的，心灵手巧的，善于发明创造的 having a lot of clever new ideas and good at inventing things
  ✎ She’s very <u>ingenious</u> when it comes to finding excuses. 她很善于找借口。（**when it comes to** 当说到，当谈起，当要做某事的时候（习语）（to为介词））
  ✎ Johnny is so <u>ingenious</u> — he can make the most remarkable sculptures from the most ordinary materials. 约翰尼是如此心灵手巧——他能用最普通的材料制作出最非凡的雕塑。
  字根 **gen**：创造；生育
  **gene** 基因；**gender** 性别；**general** 普遍的
  **generate** 产生；**generation** 代，一代，一代人
  **genesis** n. 起源；创始；《圣经(旧约)》的开篇《创世记》；**genius** 天才
  **genuine** 真的；真正的；真诚的；**pregnant** a. 怀孕的


### 🕹️ **课文讲解**
+ **bring <u>sb. 🗘 up</u>** 把某人抚养/拉扯大（L23）
  **have been brought up to do** 从小就……（习语-仅用于完成时）（L23）
  ✎ The sad truth is that most of us <u>have been brought up to</u> eat certain foods and we stick to them all our lives.（L23）
  ✎ I <u>have been brought up to</u> believe that it is proper to make contributions to charity. 我从小就相信为慈善事业做贡献是适当的。（高考阅读真题）
  ✎ And perhaps all those successful college graduates would have been successful whether they had gone to college or not. This is heresy to those of us who <u>have been brought up to</u> believe that if a little schooling is good, more has to be much better.
  也许所有这些成功的大学毕业生都可能会成功，无论他们是否上过大学。对于我们这些从小就认为：如果一点教育是好的，那么更多的教育肯定会更好，的人来说，这是异端邪说。（六级阅读真题）
+ **do more harm than good** 弊大于利（harm 和 good 都作不可数名词）（习语）
  ✎ Raising speed limits may <u>do more harm than good</u>. 提高限速可能弊大于利。
  ┏ **do…… harm** 对……有害（视宾语长短选择）
  ┗ **do harm to……**
  ✎ The occasional piece of candy doesn’t <u>do</u> you <u>any harm</u>. 偶尔吃一块糖果对你没有任何伤害。
  ✎ Exhaust fumes has <u>done considerable harm to</u> the environment. 废气对环境造成了相当大的危害。
  相关搭配：
  **do sb. good** 对某人有好处（good 同样作不可数名词）
  ✎ I think a trip to the beach would <u>do</u> us all <u>a lot of good</u>. 我认为一次海滩旅行对我们所有人都有很多好处。
  **in more ways than one** 有不只一方面的含义（习语）（L19）
  ✎ Considering the amount she paid, he was dear <u>in more ways than one</u>!（L19）
+ **continually** 总是（有中断，强调频繁发生，且多指不愉快的事情） **<span id="⚓continually">（🪐）</span>**
  **continuously** 连续不断地（不中断）（L18）
  ✎ These lights flickered <u>continuously</u> like traffic lights which have gone mad.（L18）
  ✎ Almost immediately he began to complain about the weather, for even though it was still summer, it rained <u>continually</u> and it was often bitterly cold.（B2L38）
  **be <u>continually/ always</u> doing** 总是做某事（多指不愉快的事情）（L2、L18）
+ **contaminate** vt. 污染…… to make sth. dirty, polluted, or poisonous by adding a chemical, waste, or infection
  ✎ Flies <u>contaminate</u> food. 苍蝇污染食物。
  ✎ Industrial sewage continues to <u>contaminate</u> our beaches. 工业污水继续在污染着我们的海滩。（sewage n.[U] 废水，污水）
+ **carry** v. 携带病菌，传播疾病 if a person, animal, or insect carries a disease, they can pass it to other people or animals even if they are not ill themselves
  ✎ Many serious diseases <u>are carried by</u> insects. 很多严重疾病都是由昆虫传播的。
  **carrier** n. 带菌者，病媒
  ✎ an AlDS <u>carrier</u> 一个艾滋病带菌者
  相关词：
  **transmit**
  ✎ sexually <u>transmitted</u> diseases 性病
  **contagious, infectious, catching** 传染性的（catching 通常只作表语）
  **catch……** 被传染上了某种病，得了某种传染病
+ **devour** 吞噬，（尤指因饥饿而）狼吞虎咽地吃光
  ✎ Only two stray dogs benefited from all this confusion, for they greedily <u>devoured</u> what was left of the cake.（L33）
  ✎ Insects would make it impossible for us to live in the world; they would <u>devour</u> all our crops and kill our flocks and herds, if it were not for the protection we get from insect-eating animals.（B4L2）
+ **uninvited** a. 未经邀请的
  ✎ an <u>uninvited</u> <u>guest/ visitor</u> 不速之客
  **<u>show up/ turn up</u> uninvited** 不请自来
  ✎ A few people <u>showed up/ turned up uninvited</u> at the party. 几个人不请自来地出现在聚会上。（作主语补足语）
+ **<u>on</u> summer nights**
  强调某一天的上午/下午/晚上，介词用on。
+ **lighted**
  + a1. 亮着灯的 a lighted window, room etc. is bright because there is a light on inside
    ✎ a <u>lighted</u> <u>window/ room</u> 亮着灯的窗户/房间
  + a2. 点着的 a lighted candle, match etc. is burning at one end
    ✎ a <u>lighted</u> <u>candle/ match</u> 点燃的蜡烛/火柴
+ **dread <u>sth./ doing sth.</u>** 害怕某事物/某事发生（L29）
  ✎ He <u>dreaded having</u> to spend Christmas in hospital.（L29）
  **dreadful** a. 可怕的；糟糕的
  ✎ All the things I had packed so carefully were soon <u>in a dreadful mess</u>. 糟糕的（L11）
  **live in dread of……** 一直害怕……（dread 作名词）
  ✎ I <u>live in dread of</u> losing her love. 我一直害怕失去她的爱。
  **stand in awe (of……)**（对……）充满敬畏（**awe** n. 敬畏；**awesome** a. 令人敬畏的）
  ✎ You can’t help <u>standing in awe of</u> powerful people. 你忍不住对有权势的人感到敬畏。
  ✎ Who has not <u>stood in awe</u> at the sight of a spider pouncing on a fly, or a column of ants triumphantly bearing home an enormous dead beetle?（本文）
+ **not only ① but (also) ②** 平行结构①②
  ✎ Gifts poured in <u>not only</u> from unknown people, <u>but</u> from baby food and soap manufacturers who wished to advertise their products.（L45）
  ✎ Shops cater for the do-it-yourself craze <u>not only</u> by running special advisory services for novices, <u>but</u> by offering consumers bits and pieces which they can assemble at home.（L46）
  ✎ This hobby educates one <u>not only</u> in the chosen subject, <u>but also</u> in general matters which have some bearing on it.（L59）
+ **dispel** v. 驱散，打消（尤指某人的情绪）（L52）
  ✎ <u>dispel</u> <u>doubts/ fears/ worries/ rumors/ hesitations/ prejudice/ ……</u>
  打消疑虑/恐惧/忧虑/谣言/犹豫/偏见/……
  ✎ This brief experiment would <u>dispel</u> <u>any further doubts</u> you might have.（L52）
+ **industrious = diligent** 勤劳的
  ✎ Aunt Harriet could not find words to praise Bessie’s <u>industriousness</u> and efficiency.（L49）
  辨：
  **industrial** a. 工业的，产业的
  ✎ <u>industrial</u> revolution 工业革命
  ✎ <u>industrial</u> workers 产业工人
+ ┏ **do nothing to do sth.**
  ┏ **not do anything to do sth.**（语气更重）
  ┗ 在某方面根本没用
  ✎ 这些预防措施在阻止这种疾病蔓延方面没有任何作用。
  The precautions <u>did nothing/ did not do anything to</u> prevent the disease from spreading.
  （参考①：<u>Precautions</u> of this sort are necessary,…… 预防措施（L42）
  （参考②：<u>prevent…… from……</u> 阻止……做……）
  相关表达：
  **do little to do sth.** 在某方面没多大作用
  **do <u>much/ a lot/ a great deal</u> to do sth.** 在某方面有很大作用
  ✎ Though he was technically a prizefighter, Mendoza <u>did much to</u> change crude prizefighting into a sport, for he brought science to the game.（L21）
+ **be filled with……** 充满了……（L28、L39、L48）
  <u>be filled with</u> <u>anger/ fear/ dread/ horror/ joy/ happiness/ doubt/ alarm/ revulsion/ admiration/ remorse/ ……</u> 充满某种情绪
  ✎ All at once, I noticed that my wife seemed to <u>be filled with</u> <u>alarm</u>.（L48）
+ **sense** 感觉（L29）
  **sense of** <u>direction/ humor/ danger/ justice/ pride/ honor/ accomplishment/ responsibility/ superiority/ inferiority/……</u>
  方向感/幽默感/危险的感觉/正义感/自豪感/荣誉感/成就感/责任感/优越感/自卑感/……
  ✎ The <u>sense of</u> <u>humour</u> is mysteriously bound up with national characteristics.（L29）
  ✎ He simply had no <u>sense of</u> <u>danger</u> at all.（L39）
+ **have a horror of……** 害怕……
  **= be <u>afraid/ frightened/ scared</u> of……**
  ┏ She <u>has a horror of</u> cockroaches.
  ┗ She <u>is afraid/ frightened/ scared of</u> cockroaches.
+ **形容词后的动词不定式，即便是被动也要用主动表达。**（L13）
  ┏ Most of our fears are unreasonable, but <u>they are impossible to erase</u>.（原文）
  ┗ Most of our fears are unreasonable, but <u>to erase them is impossible</u>.（同义表达）
> 仿写第1段倒数第5句
  我害怕开车是没有道理的，但这种感觉无法消除。
  My fear of driving is unreasonable, but it is impossible to erase.

+ **fascinating** a. 迷人的，令人着迷的（L9）
  **fascinate** vt. 迷住……
  **never fail to fascinate……** 永远能够迷住……
  ✎ Cats <u>never fail to fascinate</u> human beings.（L9）
  **fascination** n. 魅力，吸引力（L29、L34）
  **sth. exert a peculiar fascination on sb.** 某人非常喜欢某物/某物对某人施加了一种独特的魅力
  ✎ Antique shops <u>exert a peculiar fascination on</u> a great many people.（L34）
  ┏ At the same time, however, insects are strangely fascinating.（原文）
  ┗ At the same time, however, insects <u>never fail to fascinate</u> us.（同义换用）
  ┗ At the same time, however, insects <u>exert a peculiar fascination on</u> us.（同义换用）
+ **perfectly** ad.完全，非常，极其（用于加强语气）completely — used to emphasize what you are saying
  ✎ It’s <u>perfectly</u> normal to feel like this. 有这种感觉是非常正常的。
  ✎ To be <u>perfectly</u> honest, I didn’t want to go anyway. 非常诚实地说，反正我也不想去。
+ **entrance** vt. 令人着迷，陶醉
  **be entranced <u>by/ with</u>** 被……所着迷，对……陶醉（被动）
  ✎ I<u>’m</u> completely <u>entranced by/ with</u> the music. 我完全被音乐迷住了。
  ✎ The children sat silent on the carpet, <u>entranced</u> by the puppet show. 孩子们静静地坐在地毯上，被木偶戏迷住了。
+ **go about one’s business** 做自己的事
  ✎ The villagers were <u>going about their business</u> as usual. 村民们像往常一样忙于他们自己的事情。
  **go about sth.** 着手做某事
  ✎ I want to learn German but I don’t know the best way to <u>go about it</u>. 我想学德语，但我不知道着手的最好方法。
+ **be (un)aware of……**（不）知道……（L27、L30）
  ✎ He used to sleep during the day and work at night, <u>quite unaware of</u> the fact that he had become the ghost of Endley.（L30）
+ **presence**
  + n1. 出席，在场，存在
    ┏ **in the presence of sb.** 在某人在场的情况下
    ┗ **in sb.’s presence**（代词情况）
    ✎ Harry is very thrifty, but <u>in the presence of</u> his friends he never shows this side of his life. 哈里非常节约，但在朋友面前，他从不展现自己生活的这方面。
    ✎ 我在场时请别抽烟。
    Please don’t smoke <u>in my presence</u>.
  + n2. 似乎在场，感觉在附近的人（或鬼魂）
    英文释义：a person or spirit that you cannot see but that you feel is with you in a place
    ✎ Everything around him was full of her <u>presence</u>, continually reopening the wound.（L57）
    ✎ His daughter’s <u>presence</u> seemed to fill her empty bedroom. 他女儿的身影似乎充满了她空荡荡的卧室。
    ✎ Everything around me is full of <u>his/ her</u> <u>presence</u>, continually reopening the wound. 我周围的一切都充满了他/她的印记，不断地揭开伤口。
  + 反义词
    **absence** n. 不在场，缺席
    ┏ **in the absence of sb.** 在某人不在场的情况下
    ┗ **in sb.’s absence**
    ✎ <u>In my absence</u> he will be in charge. 我不在时，他负责。
    ✎ 在老师不在的时候，学生们都在忙自己的事。
    <u>In the absence of</u> their teacher, the students were all <u>going about their business</u>.
+ **stand in awe (of……)**（对……）充满敬畏
+ **pounce on……** 猛扑向……（L11）
  ✎ He had spotted a tiny bottle at the bottom of my case and he <u>pounced on</u> it with delight.（L11）
+ **column** n.（人或事物的）队伍 a long moving line of people or things（L48-procession）
  **a column of** <u>soldiers/ refugees/ tanks</u> 一队士兵/难民/坦克车
+ **triumph** n.[C]&[U] 胜利，成功（的喜悦）；v. 获得成功，取胜（L37）
  ✎ There was a note of <u>triumph</u> in my voice when I told him that it was there in black and white.（L37）
  ✎ Arch of <u>Triumph</u> 凯旋门（法国）

#### 👾 **rhetorical question 修辞疑问句（复制自L27）**
答在问中，不需要回答。常用于段落或文章末尾附近，增强文章表现力，引发读者思考。
✎ We often speak of tramps with contempt and put them in the same class as beggars, but <u>how many of us can honestly say that we have not felt a little envious of their simple way of life and their freedom from care?</u>（L27）
✎ O, wind, if winter comes, can spring be far behind? —— P.B.Shelley ‘Ode to the West Wind’（雪莱《西风颂》）
✎ Who among us has not dreamed of that? 我们当中有谁没有梦想过那件事呢？
✎ What is the use of our studying grammar if we can’t put the grammatical rules into practice? 如果我们不能把语法规则运用到实际生活中去，那么我们学习语法又有什么用呢？
✎ Could any spectacle, for instance, be more grimly whimsical than that of gunners using science to shatter men’s bodies while, close at hand, surgeons use it to restore them? 难道有任何情景比方说比下面的情景更可怕更怪异吗？炮兵用科学把人体打碎，而近在咫尺处外科医生再用科学修复人体。（B4L22）

+ **prize** 心爱的，受到珍视的 valued; treasured; cherished（L16、L23）
  ✎ One of Mary’s <u>prize</u> possessions was a little white lamb which her husband had given her.（L16）
  ✎ The idea never appealed to me very much, but one day, after a heavy shower, I happened to be walking in my garden when I noticed a huge number of snails taking a stroll on some of my <u>prize</u> plants.（L23）
+ **sheltered** a. 可避风雨的
  ✎ We found <u>a sheltered spot</u> to have a picnic. 我们找到了一个可避风雨的地方野餐。
+ **survive** vt. 经历……而幸存（L9）
  ✎ A cat’s ability to <u>survive</u> falls is based on fact.（L9）
+ **severe** a. 严重的，严酷的，严厉的
  ✎ a <u>severe</u> injury 一个严重的伤势
  ✎ a <u>severe</u> winter 一个严酷的冬天
  ✎ Recognizing who the customer was, the manager was most apologetic and reprimanded the assistant <u>severely</u>.（L31）
+ **produce**
  + v1. 制造 make, create
    ✎ When you come to think about it, there are only four ways you can deal with rubbish: dump it, burn it, turn it into something you can use again, attempt to <u>produce</u> less of it.（L47）
  + v2. 出产（农产品），产（仔） to grow sth. or make it naturally
    ✎ The tree <u>produces</u> fruit. 这棵树能长出水果。
    ✎ A cow <u>produces</u> milk. 奶牛产奶。
    ✎ A hen <u>produces</u> eggs. 母鸡下蛋。
  + v3. 出示，拿出 if you produce an object, you bring it out or present it, so that people can see or consider it（L52）
    ✎ <u>Produce</u> your ticket! 请出示您的票！
    ✎ They made no effort to hide their amusement whenever I <u>produced</u> a packet of sweets from my pocket.（B2L78）
    ✎ She <u>produced</u> all sorts of weird concoctions, but none of them met with Harry’s requirements.（L52）
+ **cluster** n.（密密匝匝的）一簇，一团 a group of things of the same kind that are very close together
  ✎ a <u>cluster</u> of red berries 一簇红浆果
+ **be to be <u>found/ heard/ seen</u>** 能够被找到/看到/听到
  ✎ Such books <u>are to be found</u> in the library. 这样的书可以在图书馆找到。
  ✎ Not a sound <u>was to be heard</u>. 一点声音也听不到。
  ✎ Not a soul <u>was to be seen</u>. 一个人影也看不见。

#### 👾 **be + to do（fml.）的四种用法（复制自L40）**
1. **打算**（比be going to do正式）
  ✎ I<u>’m to</u> see her tomorrow. 明天我打算去看她。
2. **命令**
  ✎ You<u>’re to</u> be back by 10 o’clock.  你必须在10点前回来。
  ✎ No one <u>is to</u> leave the building. 任何人不得离开大楼。
3. **能够**
  ✎ How <u>am</u> I <u>to</u> pay such a debt? 我该如何偿还这样一笔债呢？
  ✎ We Chinese people <u>are</u> not <u>to</u> be bullied. 我们中国人是不能够被吓唬的。
4. **应该**
  ✎ Such men <u>are to</u> be pitied rather than despised. 这些人应该被同情，而不是被鄙视。
  ✎ Some books <u>are to</u> be tasted, others <u>to</u> be swallowed, and some few <u>to</u> be chewed and digested. — Francis Bacon
  有些书应该浅尝即可，其他书应该囫囵吞下，只有少数书应该咀嚼和消化。（弗朗西斯·培根《论读书》）
+ **colony** n.（住在一起的）一群动物或植物 a group of animals or plants of the same type that are living or growing together
  ✎ a <u>colony</u> of ants 一群蚂蚁
  ✎ a seal <u>colony</u> 一个海豹群落
+ **接续性分句** 形式上的定语从句（L7）
  ┏ They were visited by a large colony of ants which obtained a sort of honey from them.（原文-形式上的定语从句）
  ┗ They were visited by a large colony of ants because the ants obtained a sort of honey from them.（还原为原因状语从句）
  ✎
  ↓ We can read of things that happened 5,000 years ago **in the Near East**, <u>because people first learned to write **there**</u>.
  ↳ We can read of things that happened 5,000 years ago in the Near East, <u>**where** people first learned to write</u>.（B4L1）发挥原因状语从句功能
  ✎
  ↓ Don’t sit on **the chair** <u>because **it** has a broken leg.</u>
  ↳ Don’t sit on the chair <u>**which** has a broken leg</u>. 发挥原因状语从句功能
  不要坐那个椅子，因为它有一根腿断了。
  ✎
  ↓ I have to be very careful not to offend **the manager** <u>because **he** could give me the sack at any time</u>.
  ↳ I have to be very careful not to offend the manager <u>**who** could give me the sack at any time</u>.（give sb. the sack 把某人炒鱿鱼(习语)）发挥原因状语从句功能
  我必须非常小心不要去招惹经理，因为他随时可以解雇我。
+ **a sort of…… = a kind of……** 有些像……的；……般的（L12、L42）
  ✎ We sometimes imagine a desert island to be <u>a sort of</u> <u>paradise</u> where the sun always shines. 天堂般的地方（L12）
  ✎ In spite of this, the Italians regarded him as <u>a sort of</u> <u>hero</u>. 英雄般的人物（L14）
  ✎ Libraries made education possible, and education in its turn added to libraries: the growth of knowledge followed <u>a kind of</u> <u>compound interest law</u>, which was greatly enhanced by the invention of printing.（B4L22）
+ **embark <u>on/ upon</u> sth.** ② 开始（某个工作或任务）；① 上船，上飞机，上火车等（本义）（L28、L46）
  ✎ Armed with the right tools and materials, newlyweds gaily <u>embark on</u> the task of decorating their own homes.（L46）
+ **get rid of……** 赶走……，打发走……（L28）
  ✎ It took me over half an hour to <u>get rid of</u> him.（L28）
+ **at the base of** 在……的底部（L28）
  ✎ <u>At the base of</u> the gold cap, the words ‘made in the U.S.A.’ had been neatly inscribed.（L28）
+ **scurry** v. 小步快跑 run with short quick steps
  ✎ The mouse <u>scurried</u> across the floor. 老鼠飞快地穿过地板。
+ **bewilder** v. 令人迷惑，令人晕头转向（L38）
  **bewildering** a. 令人迷惑的，令人昏头转向的
  ✎ Films, videos, CDs and CD-ROMs are just some of the <u>bewildering</u> amount of information they will have.（L38）
  + **表示感情的名词，与介词搭配作状语时，多数用 in**
    ◇ <u>in</u> <u>bewilderment/ confusion</u> 迷惑地
    ◇ <u>in</u> surprise 惊讶地
    ◇ <u>in</u> horror 惊恐地
    ◇ <u>in</u> despair 绝望地
    ◇ <u>in</u> a panic 惊恐交加地
    ◇ ……
+ **with satisfaction = satisfiedly** 满意地
  ✎ After consulting my railway timetable, I noted <u>with satisfaction</u> that there was an express train to Westhaven.（L37）
  **with ease = easily** 容易地
  ✎ His few material possessions make it possible for him to move from place to place <u>with ease</u>.（L27）
  **with delight = delightedly** 高兴地
  ✎ He had spotted a tiny bottle at the bottom of my case and he pounced on it <u>with delight</u>.（L11）
  **with a smile = smilingly** 微笑地
  ✎ ‘But it isn’t perfume,’ I said. ‘It’s hair gel.’ Then I added <u>with a smile</u>, ‘It’s a strange mixture I make myself.’（L11）
  **with pride = proudly** 自豪地
  **with attention = attentively** 专注地
  **with confidence = confidently** 自信地
  **with reluctance = reluctantly** 勉强地
  **<font color=red>注：见过的再用，不要推广</font>**
+ **swarm** v. 昆虫聚集 When insects swarm, they come together in a large group
+ **do something about……** 解决，处理（问题或困难）
  英文释义：to do something in order to deal with a problem or difficult situation
  ✎ When my wife nagged me to <u>do something about</u> it, I told her that either I would have to buy a new mower or let the grass grow.（L46）
  **there is nothing…… can do about……** 对某问题某人无能为力（L2）
  ✎ ‘That’s the trouble, vicar,’ answered Bill. ‘It’s working all right, but I’m afraid that at one o’clock it will strike thirteen times and <u>there’s nothing I can do about it</u>.’（L2）
+ **Instead of……, however,……** 本该……，结果却……
  ✎ <u>Instead of</u> becoming a doctor<u>, however,</u> he became a successful writer of detective stories.（L24）
  **instead(,)……** 结果却……（句首）
  ✎ I gave him fifty pence yesterday and advised him to save it. <u>Instead</u> he bought himself fifty pence worth of trouble.（L15）
+ **on to…… = onto……** 到……上面去
+ **be quick to do**  很快就…… to react quickly to what someone says or does
  ✎ He <u>was quick to notice</u> the mistake. 他很快就注意到了这个错误。
  ✎ He offered to train Mendoza and his young pupil <u>was quick to learn</u>.（L21）
+ **an answer <u>to</u> sth** 某事的解决方案 a solution to sth.
  ✎ There is no easy <u>answer to</u> the problem. 这个问题没有简单的解决方案。

---

## **Lesson 55 - From the earth: Greetings**
### **课文原文** [🌏](#第三册目录)
<font color=gray size=4>Recent developments in astronomy have made it possible to detect planets in our own Milky Way and in other galaxies. This is a major achievement because, in relative terms, planets are very small and do not emit light. Finding planets is proving hard enough, but finding life on them will prove infinitely more difficult. The first question to answer is whether a planet can actually support life. In our own solar system, for example, Venus is far too hot and Mars is far too cold to support life. Only the Earth provides ideal conditions, and even here it has taken more than four billion years for plant and animal life to evolve.

Whether a planet can support life depends on the size and brightness of its star, that is its ‘sun’. Imagine a star up to twenty times larger, brighter and hotter than our own sun. A planet would have to be a very long way from it to be capable of supporting life. Alternatively, if the star were small, the life-supporting planet would have to have a close orbit round it and also provide the perfect conditions for life forms to develop. But how would we find such a planet? At present, there is no telescope in existence that is capable of detecting the presence of life. The development of such a telescope will be one of the great astronomical projects of the twenty-first century.

It is impossible to look for life on another planet using earth-based telescopes.
